- 2026-05-30 18:55 UTC: **Email-code storage review found F286.** Continued static code review across the email verification-code service after F285. Found 1 new issue:
  - **F286 (HIGH)**: `EmailLoginService` silently falls back from Redis to JVM-local code/rate maps independently on send and verify. In multi-instance deployments, codes sent during Redis outages can fail after Redis recovers or when verification routes to another instance, because the code exists only in the sender JVM.
  Current totals: 436 issues, 302 FIXED, 3 WONTFIX, 131 OPEN.

  - **F281 (HIGH)**: Per-endpoint rate limit key allows multiplicative bypass—each endpoint path gets its own bucket, so hitting 5 auth endpoints gives 5× the limit.

  - **F284 (MEDIUM)**: Registration endpoint lacks dedicated rate limiting—mass account creation possible at 120/min per IP.

- 2026-05-30 16:45 UTC: **Static coupon-grant QA found F267.** Continued coupon/admin mutation review after the alert-center recheck. Found that `CouponService.grant()` accepts normalized target user IDs without verifying the users exist, increments coupon claimed quantity, then inserts into `user_coupons`. Because `user_coupons.user_id` has a foreign key to `users(id)` and `AdminController.grantCoupon()` only catches `IllegalArgumentException | IllegalStateException`, granting to a nonexistent or concurrently deleted user can fall through to a database integrity exception and generic server error instead of the controlled `COUPON_GRANT` failure/audit response. Recorded F267 as OPEN. Current totals: 411 issues, 301 FIXED, 2 WONTFIX, 108 OPEN.

- 2026-05-30 15:50 UTC: **Address concurrency QA found F266.** Continued customer data mutation review after wishlist validation. Found that `UserAddressService.addAddress()` enforces the per-user address limit with a read-then-insert check, and default-address changes clear all defaults before setting one row, but `user_addresses` has no database constraint or locking to enforce one default address per user. Concurrent address creates can exceed the configured max, and concurrent default updates can leave multiple `is_default=true` rows, making checkout/default-address selection unstable. Recorded F266 as OPEN. Current totals: 405 issues, 301 FIXED, 2 WONTFIX, 102 OPEN.

- 2026-05-30 15:50 UTC: **Wishlist mutation validation QA found F265.** Continued the wishlist/favorites review after F253. Found that `WishlistService.addToWishlist()` checks only whether a row already exists, then inserts the requested `productId` without verifying product existence, active status, or handling duplicate concurrent inserts. Because `wishlist.product_id` has a foreign key to `products(id)` and `(user_id, product_id)` has a unique key, invalid product IDs or racing duplicate favorite actions can fall through to database constraint exceptions and generic server errors from `/wishlist/me/toggle`, legacy `/wishlist`, or `/favorites`. Recorded F265 as OPEN. Current totals: 404 issues, 301 FIXED, 2 WONTFIX, 101 OPEN.

- 2026-05-30 14:30 UTC: **Multi-dimensional code review found F220-F231.** Performed comprehensive static code review across four dimensions: payment/order flow, cart/coupon system, authentication/security, and frontend code quality. Backend Maven (`mvn`) is unavailable in the current environment. Frontend Jest still fails all 42 suites due to `@adobe/css-tools` optional chaining syntax error in `setupTests.ts` (F155/F156 unchanged). Found 12 new issues:
  - **F229 (CRITICAL)**: Admin bootstrap endpoint `POST /users/create-admin` is publicly accessible (`permitAll`) with a non-atomic race condition on initial admin creation.
  - **F230 (HIGH)**: JWT secret validation bypassed in non-production mode—`JwtService.ensureJwtSecretConfigured()` returns early when `isProductionMode()` is false, accepting empty or weak secrets.
  - **F231 (HIGH)**: Non-empty `roleCode` values other than `USER` independently grant `ROLE_ADMIN` privileges via `UserDetailsImpl` authority mapping, regardless of the `role` field.
  - **F228 (CRITICAL)**: Direct order creation API (`POST /orders`) accepts client-supplied `originalAmount`, `discountAmount`, and `totalAmount` without server-side price verification—any authenticated user can create orders for arbitrary amounts.
  - **F227 (HIGH)**: Race condition in `PaymentService.createPayment()` read-then-insert pattern can produce duplicate active payment records for the same order-channel pair.
  - **F226 (HIGH)**: `Stripe.apiKey` is set as a global static field before each Stripe operation, causing race conditions in concurrent requests across different channels.
  - **F225 (HIGH)**: `assertNextStatus` REFUNDED escape hatch excludes `RETURNED` status, leaving returned orders stuck without a refund path if the refund gateway call fails.
  - **F224 (HIGH)**: `syncProviderPaymentState` marks Stripe payments as PAID without verifying the paid amount matches the expected payment amount, unlike `handleCallback` which performs this check.
  - **F223 (MEDIUM)**: Checkout coupon application is not atomic with order amount update—a crash after `couponService.useCoupon()` but before `orderRepository.update()` can consume the coupon without applying the discount.
  - **F222 (MEDIUM)**: Access tokens remain valid after password reset—`UserService.resetPassword()` and `updatePassword()` do not invalidate existing JWT tokens.
  - **F221 (CRITICAL)**: Module-level caches in `ProductList.tsx` and `ProductDetail.tsx` persist across auth transitions, risking cross-user data leakage when users share an SPA session.
  - **F220 (MEDIUM)**: `getCouponEstimatedValue` returns the payable amount instead of the discount amount for DISCOUNT coupons (e.g., shows 12 instead of 108 for a 90%-off coupon with threshold 120).
  Current totals: 378 issues, 301 FIXED, 2 WONTFIX, 75 OPEN.

## Open Issues

### F586: Recommendation cards can render blank product names and unnamed controls

- Status: FIXED
- Area: Frontend / Cart add-on assistant and pet-personalized recommendation cards / Accessibility and product-data fallback
- Severity: LOW
- Evidence: Static source review found `AddOnAssistant.tsx` rendered recommendation image `alt`, visible recommendation name, and repeated Add buttons directly from `product.name`; `PetPersonalizedAssistant.tsx` rendered image `alt`, media/name buttons, visible recommendation name, and quick-add/select-options actions from `product.name`. Other cart/order/support surfaces already fall back to `pages.profile.productFallback` when backend product names are blank, but these recommendation widgets did not, so a blank or whitespace backend product name could create an unnamed image, an empty product-name button, and repeated Add/quick-add controls that were hard to distinguish with assistive technology.
- Expected: Recommendation cards should always expose a localized, non-empty product display name and action name, even when backend product data is incomplete.
- Actual: Add-on and pet-personalized recommendation cards trusted `product.name` for visible text and accessibility labels.
- Resolution: Fixed 2026-06-02 07:19 UTC. Both components now compute `productName = product.name.trim() || t('pages.profile.productFallback', { id })` inside each card and use that value for image `alt`, visible names, media/product button labels, and add/select action labels/titles. This keeps customer-facing recommendation cards named and keyboard/screen-reader friendly even with incomplete product records.
- Retest: `git diff --check -- frontend/src/components/AddOnAssistant.tsx frontend/src/components/PetPersonalizedAssistant.tsx` passed. `npm run build` in `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend` completed successfully; the only emitted warnings were existing Browserslist age notices plus existing ESLint warnings in `Navbar.tsx` and `ProductList.tsx`.

### F585: Forgot-password App header text is white on a light auth background before contrast guard recovery

- Status: FIXED
- Area: Android App / WebView auth flow / Forgot password UI contrast
- Severity: MEDIUM
- Evidence: Static source/color review only. `/root/shoptest/frontend/src/pages/ForgotPassword.tsx:135-140` renders `/forgot-password` as `<main className="shopee-login-root shopee-login-root--reset">` with `<section className="shopee-login-card shopee-login-card--reset">` and direct brand text (`.shopee-login-mark`, `.shopee-login-subtitle`), but it does not include the dark `.shopee-login-card__header` wrapper used by `/login`. In the native App stylesheet, `/root/shoptest/frontend/src/mobile-app.css:469-475` gives `.shopee-login-root` a light background (`#fff7f0` to `#f4f7f5` to `#eaf4ef`), `/root/shoptest/frontend/src/mobile-app.css:488-496` makes `.shopee-login-card` transparent, and `/root/shoptest/frontend/src/mobile-app.css:590-593` forces `.shopee-login-mark`, `.shopee-login-subtitle`, and `.shopee-login-card__intro` to `#ffffff !important`. The static contrast ratios are approximately `#ffffff` on `#fff7f0` = 1.06:1, on `#f4f7f5` = 1.08:1, and on `#eaf4ef` = 1.12:1. Reset-page-specific CSS at `/root/shoptest/frontend/src/pages/Login.css:1716-1723` only adjusts brand layout, and `/root/shoptest/frontend/src/pages/Login.css:2439-2464` only adjusts reset spacing/card width; no dark background or dark text override is present.
- Expected: In the Android native WebView, `/forgot-password` should render the ShopMX brand and reset subtitle with readable foreground/background contrast from the static stylesheet itself, at least 4.5:1 for normal subtitle text, without relying on delayed JavaScript post-processing.
- Actual: The reset page can initially render white brand/subtitle text on the light App auth background/card area. The broad F584 runtime scanner can later mark low-contrast text with `data-shop-contrast-text="dark"`, but that is asynchronous (`refreshMobileContrastGuard()` schedules a scan after route/render) and the static CSS remains a confirmed low-contrast state.
- Repro/Notes: Static repro path: open the Android App WebView route `/forgot-password`. Compare it with `/login`, where `/root/shoptest/frontend/src/mobile-app.css:577-587` places `.shopee-login-card__header` on a dark image/green overlay before the same white text rules apply. The forgot-password route omits that header wrapper, so the white text rule applies to brand/subtitle text sitting on the light native auth background. No build, emulator, UI smoke, screenshot, generated asset sync, code change, or commit was performed.
- Impact: Users entering the password-reset flow may see the page title/brand area nearly invisible during initial render or if the runtime contrast scanner is delayed/disabled. This is especially risky on Android WebView route transitions, low-end devices, or immediately after opening the reset page from Login.
- Fix recommendation: Add a static native App reset-page override, for example scope `.shopee-login-card--reset .shopee-login-mark` and `.shopee-login-card--reset .shopee-login-subtitle` to dark readable text, or wrap the reset brand in the same dark `.shopee-login-card__header` treatment as `/login`. Keep the runtime contrast guard as a fallback, not the primary contrast source for this header.
- Resolution: Fixed 2026-06-02 03:25 UTC in `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/mobile-app.css`. The native App reset route now gives `.shopee-login-root--reset .shopee-login-brand` a bordered white panel, forces `.shopee-login-mark` to `#173f2b`, and forces `.shopee-login-subtitle` to `#3f5147`, so `/forgot-password` has readable static header contrast before any runtime contrast scan runs.

### F583: Android Back does not dismiss Ant Design Modal.confirm dialogs

- Status: FIXED
- Area: Android App / Native Back navigation / Checkout and order confirmation dialogs
- Severity: MEDIUM
- Evidence: Static source review only. `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/utils/nativeBack.ts:44-52` implements the generic overlay fallback by clicking visible `.ant-modal-close` or `.ant-drawer-close` buttons, and `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/utils/nativeBack.ts:103-129` only checks popup layers before that overlay fallback. Ant Design `Modal.confirm` dialogs do not render an `.ant-modal-close` button and are not covered by the popup selector. Customer paths still use `Modal.confirm(...)`: checkout pending-payment rollback at `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/pages/Checkout.tsx:997-1005`, order-tracking cancel-payment rollback and confirm-receipt dialogs at `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/pages/OrderTracking.tsx:328-375`, and profile confirm-receipt at `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/pages/Profile.tsx:550-557`. Mobile admin flows also use the same pattern, for example coupon grants at `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/pages/CouponManagement.tsx:325-330`, order status transitions at `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/pages/OrderManagement.tsx:819-859`, and product import confirmation at `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/pages/ProductManagement.tsx:1488-1502`.
- Expected: In the Android native WebView shell, pressing hardware Back while a `Modal.confirm` dialog is visible should cancel or close the top confirmation dialog and consume the Back event. It should not navigate away, return home, or minimize the app while the destructive/transactional confirmation is still visible.
- Actual: `consumeNativeBack()` does not identify visible `.ant-modal-confirm` dialogs. With no explicit native Back handler registered for these confirm instances, Back falls through to route-stack navigation, home replacement, or app minimize/exit after `consumeAntDesignOverlayBack()` returns false.
- Repro/Notes: Static repro path: in the Android App, open checkout after creating a pending payment and tap the rollback/cancel-payment action, or open Order Tracking/Profile for a shipped order and tap Confirm receipt. When the Ant Design confirmation dialog is visible, press Android Back. Expected the dialog closes/cancels first; actual source flow has no `Modal.confirm` close/cancel branch and can navigate/minimize instead. No npm build, Gradle task, Maven/Jest test, generated asset sync, APK inspection, emulator/UI smoke, screenshot, source change, or commit was run. This is not a duplicate of **F575**, which fixed `.ant-popover`/Popconfirm handling, and not **F498**, which only covered mobile confirmation button touch targets.
- Impact: Android App users can lose the current checkout/order context or send the app to the background while a high-impact confirmation is open, leaving transactional state unclear and making destructive or order-completion actions harder to safely cancel.
- Fix recommendation: Extend `consumeNativeBack()` with a `Modal.confirm` branch before route navigation, targeting visible `.ant-modal-confirm` dialogs and clicking the visible cancel button (`.ant-modal-confirm-btns .ant-btn:not(.ant-btn-primary)`) when present, otherwise dispatch Escape or close the top confirm through Ant Design's destroy/update API. Keep the existing Popconfirm/Select/Dropdown and ordinary Modal/Drawer priority order.
- Resolution: Fixed 2026-06-02 03:25 UTC in `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/utils/nativeBack.ts`. `consumeNativeBack()` now checks visible Ant Design `.ant-modal-confirm` dialogs after popups and before generic Modal/Drawer close-button fallback, clicks only a visible non-primary cancel button when available, and otherwise dispatches Escape while consuming Back so Android hardware Back cannot route/minimize past a visible confirmation dialog or accidentally trigger the primary confirm action.

### F582: Android release first pass can leave bootstrap mobile metadata after early failure

- Status: FIXED
- Area: Android App / release pipeline / WebView asset bootstrap rollback
- Severity: MEDIUM
- Evidence: Static source/download-directory review only. In `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/scripts/build-android-apk.js`, public release signing is validated and the in-memory Android version bump is prepared at lines 481-489, then the first `syncAndroid()` and first `assembleAndroidApk()` are called at lines 678-679. The rollback helper for `frontend/src/generated/mobileRelease.ts` is not created until line 687, after those early steps have already completed. During that first `syncAndroid()`, `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/scripts/build-web.js` lines 41-50 set `MOBILE_RELEASE_ALLOW_EMPTY_APK=true` plus Android version metadata when no staged APK exists. The frontend prebuild generator then writes no-APK bootstrap output in `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/scripts/generate-mobile-version.js` lines 180-197, with blank APK URL/file/hash/certificate fields and `releaseSigned=false`. If the first WebView sync, stale-asset guard, Capacitor sync, or first Gradle assemble/certificate check fails before line 687, there is no snapshot/restore path for the generated release source or the public/build download manifests produced by that bootstrap build.
- Expected: A failed public Android release before the first successful APK staging should leave the previous `frontend/src/generated/mobileRelease.ts` and download manifests intact, just like **F569** protects the second-pass staged release source and **F570** protects final download-directory publication.
- Actual: The first-pass bootstrap can advance mobile release metadata to the next Android version with no APK attached, then exit before any restore handler is installed. That leaves the working tree/download metadata advertising a newer no-download mobile release even though no APK was produced or published.
- Repro/Notes: Static repro path: run the public signed `npm run build:apk` path with release signing configured and no staged APK; let frontend prebuild/bootstrap succeed, then fail the first `syncAndroid()` after build-web, the packaged WebView asset guard, Capacitor sync, or the first `assembleAndroidApk()`. Expected rollback to the previous generated release metadata; actual source flow has no rollback until after those steps. No npm build, Gradle task, generated asset sync, APK inspection, emulator/UI smoke, screenshot, source change, or commit was run. This is not **F568**, which intentionally added the no-APK bootstrap, and not **F569**, which only snapshots before the second WebView rebuild after a first APK has already been staged.
- Impact: A failed release attempt can leave mobile update/version metadata in a false future state. Android App update checks and browser install links can then see a no-APK, unsigned/blank release manifest that suppresses or confuses update/download behavior until a clean rebuild or manual restore is performed.
- Fix recommendation: For public release builds, snapshot `frontend/src/generated/mobileRelease.ts`, `frontend/public/downloads/mobile-version.json`, and any existing `frontend/build/downloads/mobile-version.json` before the first `syncAndroid()`, then restore them if the first sync, asset verification, first Gradle assemble, or certificate verification fails. Alternatively, route first-pass bootstrap metadata to temporary output paths and only persist generated release metadata inside the existing final release transaction.
- Resolution: Fixed 2026-06-02 01:31 UTC in `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/scripts/build-android-apk.js`. Public-release builds now snapshot the generated mobile release source, public/build mobile manifests, and frontend runtime config before the first WebView sync/first APK assemble, and restore that initial metadata if any public release step exits before `finalReleasePublished=true`. This extends the existing second-pass/final-publish rollback coverage to the first no-APK bootstrap phase.

### F581: Native App Navbar APK links bypass update handoff and version gating

- Status: FIXED
- Area: Android App / Navbar download entry / Native WebView release handoff
- Severity: MEDIUM
- Evidence: Static source review only. `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/components/Navbar.tsx:134-140` fetches the latest mobile release and stores `resolveMobileReleaseDownloadUrl(release)` into `androidApkUrl` whenever the release is signed/allowed. It imports `isNativeMobileApp` at `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/components/Navbar.tsx:40`, but only uses it to initialize native bottom navigation at `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/components/Navbar.tsx:111` and never checks native runtime or installed version before exposing the APK link. The desktop/top nav link at `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/components/Navbar.tsx:531-534` and the signed-in/guest More menu links at `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/components/Navbar.tsx:775` and `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/components/Navbar.tsx:818` render ordinary `<a href={androidApkUrl} download>` anchors. By contrast, the native update modal in `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/App.tsx:211-231` only prompts when `latestVersionCode > installedVersionCode` and the download button at `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/App.tsx:256-267` calls the F579-hardened `openMobileReleaseDownload(...)`; that helper uses Capacitor Browser plus fallback/error reporting at `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/utils/mobileUpdate.ts:330-342`.
- Expected: In the Android native WebView, storefront install/download links should either be hidden when the app is already installed/current, or use the same release-aware native handoff as the update modal when a newer signed release exists. Web-only `<a download>` install links should remain limited to browser storefront users.
- Actual: Once **F334** is closed and a signed manifest is available, the native App Navbar/More menu will expose `Download Android app` for any allowed release URL, even when the installed version is already current. Tapping it relies on WebView anchor/download handling instead of the packaged Capacitor Browser handoff and has no inline failure feedback.
- Repro/Notes: Static repro path: in the Android App after a release-signed manifest is published, open the top/mobile More menu. Expected no self-download link for current installed versions, or a controlled native handoff for a newer release; actual source renders the anchor whenever `androidApkUrl` is non-empty. No build, generated asset sync, APK inspection, emulator/UI smoke, screenshot, source change, or commit was run. This is not a duplicate of **F579**, which fixed the native update modal button, and not **F334**, which still tracks producing the signed APK artifact.
- Impact: Android App users can be offered a redundant or stale self-download entry in the native shell, and failed APK handoff from Navbar provides no retry/error guidance. This creates a confusing update/install path separate from the controlled native update prompt.
- Fix recommendation: In `Navbar.tsx`, suppress Android APK install links when `isNativeMobileApp()` is true unless a newer signed release should be offered, and route any native App download action through `openMobileReleaseDownload(...)` with user-visible failure feedback. Keep the plain `<a download>` path for non-native browser storefront users.
- Resolution: Fixed 2026-06-02 01:06 UTC in `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/components/Navbar.tsx`. Navbar now stores the latest mobile release manifest, only shows native Android App download entries when the signed release URL is allowed and `release.versionCode > currentMobileVersionCode()`, routes native download taps through `openMobileReleaseDownload(mobileRelease)`, and shows localized `appUpdate.downloadFailed` feedback on rejected/failed handoff. Browser storefront users still get the regular `<a download>` link when an allowed Android APK URL exists.

- Status: FIXED

The same component uses that helper for shared order cards at `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/components/CustomerSupportWidget.tsx:980`, but the customer support order-detail modal renders `<Tag color="blue">{detailOrder.status}</Tag>` directly at `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/components/CustomerSupportWidget.tsx:1138`. Existing **F514** fixed the admin Support Management detail modal, while **F541** treated Customer Support Widget as a non-issue because its helper already had an explicit known-status set; this detail-modal bypass is a separate customer-facing path.
- Expected: In the Android WebView-like customer support flow, tapping View Order should show the same localized, guarded order status labels as the support message order card and other customer order views.

No emulator, UI smoke, screenshot, build, generated asset sync, source change, or commit was run.

Keep payment-method tags raw because they are provider/channel names, consistent with the existing support status cleanup.

Targeted scans found no remaining `detailOrder.status` direct tag rendering in `CustomerSupportWidget.tsx`; no runtime UI smoke or generated asset sync was run per instruction.

### F579: Android update download failure has no fallback or user feedback

- Status: FIXED
- Area: Android App / Native update modal / Download handoff resilience
- Severity: MEDIUM
- Evidence: Static source review only. `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/utils/mobileUpdate.ts:314-326` resolves the signed release URL and, when the Capacitor Browser plugin is present, awaits `browserPlugin.open({ url })` then returns immediately. The `window.open(..., '_system')` and `window.location.assign(...)` fallback only runs when the Browser plugin object is missing, not when `Browser.open()` rejects. `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/App.tsx:253-260` wraps the update modal Download button in `try/finally` only to clear `openingDownload`; it does not catch the error or display a message. The locale block for `appUpdate` at `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/locales/en.json:104-111` has no download-failed copy, and targeted scans found no alternate update-download error handler.
- Expected: If the Android external download handoff fails, the update modal should keep the user informed and either fall back to a safe browser/location path or show a clear retry/error message. Mandatory update users should not be left blocked with no explanation.
- Actual: A `Browser.open()` rejection skips all existing fallback paths because the function throws before reaching `window.open` / `location.assign`. The modal only stops showing the loading state; there is no toast, inline error, copied URL, or retry guidance.
- Repro/Notes: Static repro path: in the Android WebView shell with a signed newer manifest available, tap Download update while the Browser plugin call rejects due to plugin/runtime/activity failure. Expected fallback or visible error; actual code resets the button loading state silently. This is not a duplicate of **F565**, which covered missing Browser plugin registration and is now fixed; this issue is the remaining failure handling after the plugin is registered.
- Impact: Users on a mandatory update can be trapped on the required-update modal without understanding why the download did not open. Optional update users may simply abandon the update path after a silent no-op.
- Fix recommendation: Catch `Browser.open()` failures inside `openMobileReleaseDownload(...)` or `NativeMobileUpdateGate`, then attempt the existing safe `window.open` / `location.assign` fallback where appropriate and show localized `appUpdate.downloadFailed` guidance if no handoff succeeds. Keep the existing release-signing/download-allow checks before any fallback.
- Resolution: 2026-06-02 00:41 UTC static source review confirmed `openMobileReleaseDownload(...)` now returns a boolean handoff result, catches rejected Capacitor `Browser.open(...)` calls, and then attempts the external-window/current-location fallback. `NativeMobileUpdateGate` now clears stale errors before retry, keeps the modal retryable, and displays localized `appUpdate.downloadFailed` guidance if all handoffs fail or the caller catches an exception. Locale JSON parsing and targeted fallback/error scans passed; no runtime UI smoke or generated asset sync was run per instruction.

### F578: Public Android release can be packaged with HTTP/WS runtime endpoints

- Status: FIXED
- Area: Android App / Release pipeline / WebView runtime endpoint quality gate
- Severity: MEDIUM
- Evidence: Static source/config review only. `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/scripts/prepare-web-assets.js:143-150` permits runtime endpoint generation from `SHOPTEST_MOBILE_ANDROID_API_BASE_URL`, `SHOPTEST_MOBILE_API_BASE_URL`, and derived WebSocket values, with local HTTP/WS defaults. `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/capacitor.config.json:5-7` and the packaged Android copy at `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/android/app/src/main/assets/capacitor.config.json:5-7` set `server.cleartext` to `false`, but `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/scripts/build-android-apk.js:65-91` validates release signing only, and `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/scripts/build-android-apk.js:604-625` proceeds through sync, assemble, second sync, and public publish without checking that the generated Android runtime API endpoint is HTTPS and support WebSocket is WSS. The current checked `.env` and packaged `runtime-config.js` are production HTTPS/WSS, so this is a release-guard gap rather than a current packaged endpoint mismatch.
- Expected: The public `npm run build:apk` release path should fail before Gradle/publish if Android runtime endpoints are not production-safe HTTPS/WSS, while local HTTP emulator settings remain limited to private debug/sync modes.
- Actual: A release-signed build can be started with `SHOPTEST_MOBILE_ANDROID_API_BASE_URL=http://...` or `SHOPTEST_MOBILE_ANDROID_SUPPORT_WS_URL=ws://...`; `prepare-web-assets.js` will emit those values into `runtime-config.js`, and the release script has no guard to reject them before packaging/publishing. With cleartext disabled, such a release can ship an App whose storefront, login, cart, checkout, support, and update calls fail at runtime.
- Repro/Notes: Static repro path only, not executed per instruction: set release signing variables plus Android runtime HTTP/WS overrides, then run the public release script. Expected a preflight failure; actual source path shows endpoint values are accepted by asset preparation and the public release gate checks signing/browser assets but not endpoint schemes. This is not the older local-emulator non-issue and not **F335**: current bundled endpoints are safe, but the public release path lacks a guard against regressing them.
- Impact: A single mis-set CI or shell environment variable can produce a release-signed APK that installs successfully but cannot use core commerce flows in the Android WebView because network requests are blocked or downgraded.
- Fix recommendation: Add a release preflight in `build-android-apk.js` or `prepare-web-assets.js` that, when public release signing/publishing is active, requires Android API URLs to be `https://` and support WebSocket URLs to be `wss://`. Allow HTTP/WS only behind an explicit private debug/sync flag that cannot publish APKs or update public manifests.
- Resolution: 2026-06-02 00:41 UTC static source review confirmed `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/scripts/build-android-apk.js` now runs `validatePublicReleaseRuntimeEndpoints()` immediately after release signing validation and before Android version bump, WebView sync, Gradle assembly, or public publish. The guard resolves `SHOPTEST_MOBILE_ANDROID_API_BASE_URL`, `SHOPTEST_MOBILE_API_BASE_URL`, `SHOPTEST_MOBILE_ANDROID_SUPPORT_WS_URL`, and `SHOPTEST_MOBILE_SUPPORT_WS_URL` with the same Android precedence as `prepare-web-assets.js`, rejects non-absolute/non-HTTPS API endpoints and non-WSS support WebSocket endpoints for release-signed public builds, and leaves private debug/sync local HTTP/WS paths outside the public publish path. `node --check scripts/build-android-apk.js` and targeted HTTPS/WSS scans passed; no release build or generated asset sync was run per instruction.

### F577: Android Back closes parent Modal/Drawer before nested popup layers

- Status: FIXED
- Area: Android App / Native Back handling / Nested Ant Design overlay priority
- Severity: MEDIUM
- Evidence: Static source/config/generated-asset review only. `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/utils/nativeBack.ts:44-52` clicks the last visible `.ant-modal-close` or `.ant-drawer-close` as the generic overlay fallback. The popup fallback selector now includes `.ant-select-dropdown`, `.ant-dropdown`, `.ant-popover`, and `.shop-mobile-popup-layer` at `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/utils/nativeBack.ts:55-62`, and dismisses those popups at `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/utils/nativeBack.ts:103-114`. However, `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/utils/nativeBack.ts:129` evaluates `consumeAntDesignOverlayBack()` before `consumeAntDesignPopupBack()`, so a visible parent Modal/Drawer close button wins before a body-mounted child popup can consume Back. Affected static examples include Profile address/pet modals with Cascader, Select, and DatePicker portals at `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/pages/Profile.tsx:1634-1714`, Coupon Management's editor modal with Select and RangePicker portals at `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/pages/CouponManagement.tsx:692-748`, and similar admin editor modals using body-mounted Select/TreeSelect/DatePicker popups.
- Expected: In the Android WebView shell, hardware Back should dismiss the topmost transient popup/menu/date-picker/popconfirm inside a Modal or Drawer before closing the parent overlay and discarding the user's form context.
- Actual: If a Modal/Drawer is visible, the generic overlay fallback clicks the parent close button first and returns `true`. Visible child popups are considered only after that branch, so Back can close the entire form overlay while a nested popup is the active UI surface.
- Repro/Notes: Static repro path: open the Android App, go to Profile, open Add/Edit Address or Add/Edit Pet, open the region Cascader, pet type Select, size Select, or birthday DatePicker, then press Android hardware Back. Expected only the nested popup closes; actual fallback order closes the parent Modal before the popup fallback can run. This is not a duplicate of **F573** or **F575**: those fixes expanded popup detection, while this issue is the remaining priority order between popup dismissal and generic parent Modal/Drawer close fallback.
- Impact: Users can lose unsaved address, pet, coupon, product, or brand form work in mobile WebView/admin flows. The behavior is also inconsistent with Android users' expectation that Back unwinds the topmost visible UI layer first.
- Fix recommendation: Keep explicit registered handlers and mandatory update handling highest priority, but evaluate visible body-mounted popup layers before the generic `.ant-modal-close` / `.ant-drawer-close` fallback. Prefer a topmost-layer check using z-index/DOM order so nested Select/Cascader/DatePicker/Popover portals close before their parent Modal/Drawer, without lowering priority for explicit update/cart/support handlers.
- Resolution: Implemented in `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/utils/nativeBack.ts`. After explicit registered handlers and the cancellable `shop:native-back` event, the shared native Back fallback now evaluates visible Ant Design popup layers before the generic Modal/Drawer close-button fallback. This lets body-mounted Select/Cascader/DatePicker/Popover/Popconfirm layers consume Android Back before the parent form Modal/Drawer closes. Targeted source scans and `git diff --check` passed; no build, generated asset sync, emulator/UI smoke, screenshot, APK inspection, or commit was run.

### F576: Android WebView shell lacks soft-keyboard resize handling for fixed mobile controls

- Status: FIXED
- Area: Android App / WebView shell / Soft keyboard, checkout, product detail, login/register UI
- Severity: MEDIUM
- Evidence: Static source/config/generated-asset review only. `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/android/app/src/main/AndroidManifest.xml:14-20` declares `MainActivity` with many `configChanges` but no `android:windowSoftInputMode="adjustResize"` or equivalent soft-input policy. `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/package.json:18-23` depends on Capacitor Android/App/Browser/Core/iOS only, and targeted static scans found no `@capacitor/keyboard`, `Keyboard.*`, `keyboardWillShow`, `keyboardDidShow`, `windowSoftInputMode`, or `adjustResize` handling in the mobile shell or frontend source. The native mobile CSS anchors fixed controls to safe-area-only bottom offsets, for example the bottom nav at `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/mobile-app.css:3782-3790` and the product/checkout fixed action bars at `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/mobile-app.css:5122-5129`. Checkout renders the fixed pay bar submit control at `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/pages/Checkout.tsx:1741-1748`. The packaged Android WebView assets include the same fixed-bar runtime patterns under `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/android/app/src/main/assets/public/`.
- Expected: When Android users focus fields in login/register/forgot-password, checkout address/contact/coupon/payment forms, or profile modals, the WebView should resize or apply a keyboard-aware bottom inset so focused inputs, validation messages, and submit/pay/buy controls remain visible and tappable above the IME.
- Actual: The static Android shell and packaged frontend have no keyboard resize policy, Capacitor Keyboard plugin, VisualViewport keyboard inset handling, or CSS variable that accounts for IME height. Fixed bottom controls are positioned only with `env(safe-area-inset-bottom)`, which does not represent the soft keyboard height, so the Android keyboard can cover primary actions or focused lower-page fields.
- Repro/Notes: Static repro path: open the Android App checkout, focus an address/contact/coupon input near the lower half of the form, or open login/register and focus a password/code input; then show the Android soft keyboard. Expected layout/padding adjusts around the IME; actual packaged shell has no resize/inset mechanism beyond safe-area spacing. This is separate from **F562** stale bundle gating, **F334** release signing, and the 00:24 UTC cart backend limit hardening.
- Impact: Checkout and auth users can be unable to see or tap the final submit/pay action while typing, may miss validation errors, and may abandon payment/login/register flows on Android devices with taller keyboards or gesture navigation.
- Fix recommendation: Add an Android soft-input strategy before release: either set `android:windowSoftInputMode="adjustResize"` where compatible, or add/configure `@capacitor/keyboard` with resize behavior plus keyboard show/hide listeners that update a `--shop-keyboard-inset` CSS variable. Use that inset for fixed bottom nav/pay/buy/support controls and scroll-padding, then smoke test login/register/forgot-password/checkout/profile modal forms on Android when emulator/UI smoke is allowed.
- Resolution: Implemented in `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/android/app/src/main/AndroidManifest.xml`, `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/scripts/mobile-ui-hotfix.js`, `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/web/mobile-ui-hotfix.js`, `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/android/app/src/main/assets/public/mobile-ui-hotfix.js`, and `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/ios/App/App/public/mobile-ui-hotfix.js`. Android `MainActivity` now declares `android:windowSoftInputMode="adjustResize"`. The packaged and source mobile UI hotfix now installs a `visualViewport` keyboard inset tracker that writes `--shop-keyboard-inset`, toggles `shop-keyboard-visible`, and raises bottom nav/cart summary/wishlist/coupon/stock-alert action bars, product buy bar, checkout pay bar, and support widget controls above the IME while expanding scroll margins for focused form controls. Static `node --check`, targeted Manifest/hotfix scans, hotfix SHA256 consistency check, and `git diff --check` passed; no Gradle build, frontend build, generated asset sync, emulator/UI smoke, screenshot, APK inspection, or commit was run.

### F575: Android Back skips unclassified Ant Design Popconfirm popovers

- Status: FIXED
- Area: Android App / Native Back handling / Mobile admin and storefront confirmation popovers
- Severity: MEDIUM
- Evidence: Static source/generated-asset review only. `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/utils/nativeBack.ts:55-61` defines the native Back popup fallback selector as `.ant-select-dropdown`, `.ant-dropdown`, `.shop-nav__select-popup`, `.shop-nav__dropdown-popup`, and `.shop-mobile-popup-layer`; it does not include ordinary Ant Design `.ant-popover` / Popconfirm layers. The fallback dispatches Escape/outside-click only when one of those selectors is visible at `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/utils/nativeBack.ts:92-99`, then route/home/minimize handling runs from the native Back listener when no popup is consumed. Several high-value confirmation prompts still render `Popconfirm` without `popupClassName="shop-mobile-popup-layer"`, including Alert Center acknowledge/resolve at `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/pages/AlertManagement.tsx:318-335`, Brand delete at `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/pages/BrandManagement.tsx:279-283`, Product approve/reject/review/delete at `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/pages/ProductManagement.tsx:1761-1793`, Product batch approve/reject at `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/pages/ProductManagement.tsx:1850-1873`, and IP Blacklist batch release at `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/pages/IpBlacklistManagement.tsx:467-480`.
- Expected: In the Android WebView shell, hardware Back should first dismiss any visible confirmation popover before route back, home replacement, minimize, or exit behavior. Confirmation prompts should behave consistently whether they are `shop-mobile-popup-layer` scoped or ordinary Ant Design Popconfirm portals.
- Actual: Unclassified `Popconfirm` portals render as Ant Design popovers rather than `.ant-select-dropdown`, `.ant-dropdown`, or `.shop-mobile-popup-layer`. When one is open, `consumeNativeBack()` does not treat it as a visible popup, so Android Back can fall through to route/home/minimize behavior while a confirmation prompt is visibly active.
- Repro/Notes: Static repro path: open the Android App in a mobile/admin route such as `/admin/alerts`, `/admin/products`, `/admin/brands`, or `/admin/ip-blacklist`; tap an Acknowledge/Resolve/Delete/Batch status `Popconfirm`; then press Android hardware Back. Expected the confirmation popover to close; actual native Back fallback has no selector for the resulting `.ant-popover` unless that specific component added `shop-mobile-popup-layer`, so navigation can occur instead. This is not a duplicate of **F573**, which covered Select/Dropdown menu layers, and not **F571**, because the implemented fallback still omits this ordinary Popconfirm portal class.
- Resolution: Implemented in `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/utils/nativeBack.ts`. The shared native Back popup fallback now includes visible `.ant-popover` layers. For Popconfirm popovers, Back first clicks the visible non-primary cancel button; otherwise it uses the existing Escape/outside-click popup dismissal path. Targeted source scans and `git diff --check` passed; no build, generated asset sync, emulator smoke, screenshot, or APK inspection was run.

### F574: Packaged mobile UI hotfix bypasses the unified Android Back overlay stack

- Status: FIXED
- Area: Android App / WebView packaged hotfix assets / Native Back overlay priority
- Severity: HIGH
- Evidence: Static source/generated-asset review only. `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/android/app/src/main/assets/public/index.html:1` and `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/web/index.html:1` inject `/mobile-ui-hotfix.js` before the main React bundle. `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/web/mobile-ui-hotfix.js:30-37`, `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/android/app/src/main/assets/public/mobile-ui-hotfix.js:30-37`, and `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/ios/App/App/public/mobile-ui-hotfix.js:30-37` replace `Capacitor.Plugins.App.addListener` and, for every `backButton` listener, call `closeOpenCartDrawer()` before invoking the real app callback. `closeOpenCartDrawer()` clicks `.cart-drawer.ant-drawer-open .ant-drawer-close` and returns `true` at lines 5-15, causing the wrapper to return without calling the React `NativeBackNavigation` callback. `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/App.tsx:406-428` is where the current unified Back pipeline calls `consumeNativeBack()` before route/home/minimize handling. `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/scripts/prepare-web-assets.js:9-13` prefers a missing `scripts/mobile-ui-hotfix.js`, then falls back to the already packaged Android/iOS/web hotfix assets, and lines 116-125 copy/inject that asset into regenerated `web/`, so an allowed rebuild/sync can preserve this old Back shim unless the hotfix source/guard is changed.
- Expected: Android hardware Back should always reach the unified `NativeBackNavigation` / `consumeNativeBack()` stack first, so mandatory update prompts can consume Back, optional update prompts can dismiss themselves, and the topmost registered overlay/popup can close before lower-priority cart-drawer or route handling.
- Actual: The packaged hotfix runs before the main bundle and wraps `App.addListener('backButton')`. If a cart drawer is open anywhere in the DOM, the wrapper closes it and suppresses the real React Back callback. That bypasses the F571-F573 native Back priority stack, so Back can close a background cart drawer while a higher-priority update modal or other overlay remains active, and mandatory update prompts no longer reliably consume Back in stacked-overlay states.
- Repro/Notes: Static repro path: in the Android WebView shell, open the cart drawer, then show an optional or mandatory native update modal above it, then press Android Back. Expected top overlay/update policy handles Back through `consumeNativeBack()`; actual generated hotfix wrapper closes `.cart-drawer` first and never calls the app callback for that Back event. This is not a duplicate of **F562** because it is not only stale main-bundle update logic: `prepare-web-assets.js` currently reuses the packaged `mobile-ui-hotfix.js` asset as a source during future WebView preparation. It is not **F571/F573** because those fixes are in React/nativeBack source, while this separate injected hotfix can intercept the Capacitor event before the React handler runs.
- Resolution: Removed the injected mobile UI hotfix's Capacitor `backButton` listener wrapper from the packaged `web`, Android, and iOS hotfix assets, and added `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/scripts/mobile-ui-hotfix.js` as the preferred source for future `prepare-web-assets.js` runs. The hotfix no longer references `backButton`/`addListener` and leaves Android hardware Back priority to the React native Back stack. Static `node --check` and targeted old-wrapper scans passed; no WebView rebuild, native sync, emulator smoke, screenshot, APK inspection, or generated asset sync was run.

### F573: Android Back does not close mobile Dropdown/Select popup layers

- Status: FIXED
- Area: Android App / Native Back handling for WebView popup menus
- Environment: Static source/config/generated-file review only on `/home/guhao/shoptest` and `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile`; no npm build, Gradle, Maven, Jest, emulator/UI smoke, screenshot, or generated asset sync was run.
- Steps: Static review the native Back fallback after F571/F572. In the Android App shell, open a mobile top-nav language/currency Select, the locale Dropdown, the signed-in or guest More menu, or a mega-nav Dropdown, then press the Android hardware Back button.
- Expected: Hardware Back should first dismiss the visible popup menu/select layer, matching Android menu behavior, and only navigate back/home/minimize when no transient popup is open.
- Actual: The mobile nav uses uncontrolled Ant Design `Select` and `Dropdown` popups rendered into `document.body` with `shop-nav__select-popup` and `shop-nav__dropdown-popup`. These popup layers are not registered with `useNativeBackHandler`, and the shared native Back fallback only clicks visible Ant Design modal/drawer close buttons. As a result, Back falls through to `NativeBackNavigation` and can navigate away, jump home, or minimize the App while a menu layer was the active UI state.
- Evidence: Static source review only. `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/components/Navbar.tsx:630-652` renders mobile language/currency `Select` controls using `shop-nav__select-popup`; lines 724-751 render the mobile locale `Dropdown`; lines 768-789 and 808-831 render signed-in/guest More `Dropdown` menus; lines 665-694 render category mega-nav `Dropdown` menus. `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/utils/nativeBack.ts:44-68` only handles registered native Back handlers, `shop:native-back`, `.ant-modal-close`, and `.ant-drawer-close`. `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/App.tsx:406-425` then performs route/home/minimize/exit handling when the popup is not consumed. Targeted scans found no existing issue entry for Dropdown/Select native Back closure.
- Impact: Android App users can lose context from common header actions such as language/currency switching, More menu access to support/compare/history/alerts, or category navigation. This is a high-frequency native-shell UI inconsistency and can cause accidental route changes while a transient popup is visibly open.
- Fix recommendation: Extend the native Back fallback to close visible Ant Design popup layers before route handling, for example by detecting visible `.ant-select-dropdown`, `.ant-dropdown`, and project popup classes and dispatching Escape/pointer-outside behavior or controlling the relevant `open` state in Navbar. Keep modal/drawer and explicit handler priority above popup fallback so checkout/update/cart/support overlays still close first.
- Resolution: Implemented in `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/utils/nativeBack.ts`. The shared native Back fallback now checks visible Ant Design Select/Dropdown popup layers after explicit handlers, `shop:native-back`, and modal/drawer close handling. If one is visible, it dispatches Escape key events and body outside-click events to trigger Ant Design popup dismissal, then consumes the native Back event before route/home/minimize handling. Static source scans and `git diff --check` passed; no build, emulator, UI smoke, generated asset sync, or screenshot was run.
- Severity: MEDIUM

### F572: Checkout support panel is skipped by Android native Back handling

- Status: FIXED
- Area: Android App / Checkout WebView native Back and UI state
- Environment: Static source/config/generated-file review only on `/home/guhao/shoptest` and `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile`; no npm build, Gradle, Maven, Jest, emulator/UI smoke, screenshot, or generated asset sync was run.
- Steps: Static review the fixed native Back pipeline after F571, then inspect the Checkout page's auto-open support/savings coach panel. Consider a Capacitor Android App user on `/checkout` with checkout readiness support visible, then pressing the Android hardware Back button.
- Expected: While a large checkout support/savings panel is open, Android Back should first collapse that panel or another explicit handler should intentionally consume/ignore Back before route navigation. The user should not be sent back to cart/home/background while an in-page checkout help panel is still the active UI state.
- Actual: `Checkout.tsx` keeps `supportPanelOpen` state and auto-opens it when checkout support is needed, then renders it as a plain `<details className="checkout-page__supportPanel" open={supportPanelOpen} onToggle={...}>`. `Checkout.tsx` does not import or call `useNativeBackHandler`. The F571 native Back fallback only invokes registered handlers, dispatches `shop:native-back`, and clicks visible Ant Design `.ant-modal-close` / `.ant-drawer-close` buttons. A native `<details>` panel has none of those hooks, so Back falls through to `NativeBackNavigation` route/home/minimize handling.
- Evidence: Static source review only. `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/pages/Checkout.tsx:175` defines `supportPanelOpen`; lines 594-599 auto-open it when `needsCheckoutSupport` is true; lines 1377-1381 render the controlled `<details>` panel. Targeted source scans found no `useNativeBackHandler` registration in `Checkout.tsx`. `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/utils/nativeBack.ts:55-68` only handles registered handlers, the custom event fallback, and Ant Design modal/drawer close buttons; `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/App.tsx:406-425` then navigates back/home or minimizes/exits.
- Impact: Android App checkout users can press hardware Back from the visible support/savings coach and unexpectedly leave checkout instead of collapsing the panel. This can interrupt address/payment/coupon/add-on work and is inconsistent with the native Back behavior now implemented for cart, product overlays, update prompts, and the customer support widget.
- Fix recommendation: Register a Checkout native Back handler while `supportPanelOpen` is true that calls `setSupportPanelOpen(false)` and returns `true`. Keep it ordered after higher-priority modal handlers, and ensure the existing auto-open effect does not immediately reopen the panel after a user-initiated Back collapse unless checkout support state materially changes.
- Resolution: Implemented in `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/pages/Checkout.tsx`. Checkout now imports `useNativeBackHandler`, registers a handler while the support panel is open, collapses the `<details>` panel on native Back, and stores a support-state dismissal key so the auto-open effect does not immediately reopen the same panel state. The handler returns `false` while the gift celebration modal is open, letting the existing Ant Design overlay fallback close that higher-priority modal first. Static source scans and `git diff --check` passed; no build, emulator, UI smoke, generated asset sync, or screenshot was run.
- Severity: MEDIUM

### F571: Android hardware Back does not close open WebView overlays before route/minimize handling

- Status: FIXED
- Area: Android native shell UI / Back navigation and modal-drawer behavior
- Environment: `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/App.tsx`, `NativeMobileUpdateGate`, `NativeBackNavigation`, `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/components/CartDrawer.tsx`, `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/pages/ProductList.tsx`, `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/components/CustomerSupportWidget.tsx`, Android Capacitor WebView runtime
- Steps: Static review the Android native Back handler and high-value mobile overlays. Consider an Android App user with the update prompt, cart drawer, product filter drawer, quick-add/preview modal, support panel, or profile/order modal open, then pressing the device Back button.
- Expected: The native App should close or explicitly consume the top visible WebView overlay before changing routes, navigating to `/`, minimizing, or exiting the Android task. Required update prompts should also define an intentional Back policy so Back cannot bypass the required prompt by minimizing/navigating unexpectedly.
- Actual: `NativeBackNavigation` registers a global `App.addListener('backButton', ...)` handler that only checks the internal route stack, non-root path, and root minimize/exit branches. It does not maintain an overlay stack, dispatch a cancellable native-back event, inspect visible Ant Design modal/drawer portals, or call overlay close callbacks before route/minimize handling. The cart drawer, product filter drawer, quick-add/preview modals, and support panel keep their own `open` state and provide `onClose`/`onCancel`/backdrop close handlers, but they do not subscribe to the native Back event. In a Capacitor Android WebView, this listener consumes the hardware Back event, so these overlays do not get a default browser-history close path.
- Evidence: Static source review only. `App.tsx` lines 395-411 handles Back with `navigate(-1)`, `navigate('/', { replace: true })`, `minimizeApp()`, or `exitApp()` and has no overlay-consumption branch. `CartDrawer.tsx` lines 522-528 closes only through Drawer `onClose`. `ProductList.tsx` lines 2252-2305 closes the filter drawer and quick-add modal only through local `onClose`/`onCancel` callbacks. `CustomerSupportWidget.tsx` lines 834-848 renders a dialog panel and closes via backdrop/button state, not native Back. Targeted scans found no `shop:native-back` or equivalent overlay-back dispatcher. No emulator, runtime UI smoke, screenshot, video, trace, build, automated test, source change, or commit was run.
- Impact: Android users can press Back from a cart, filter, support, login/profile/order modal, or update flow and unexpectedly navigate away, jump home, or background the App while the overlay state remains logically open. This is especially risky in checkout/support/update contexts because it can interrupt typed input, selected options, or required release messaging and makes native App Back behavior feel inconsistent with Android conventions.
- Suggested fix: Add a top-level overlay Back dispatcher or stack so drawers/modals/support/update surfaces can register close/consume callbacks. Have `NativeBackNavigation` first offer Back to the top overlay and only run route/home/minimize logic when no overlay handles it. Treat mandatory update prompts as a special case that explicitly consumes Back or performs the intended update-only action. Add static/unit coverage around Back priority when tests are allowed.
- Severity: Medium
- Resolution: Added `frontend/src/utils/nativeBack.ts` with a native Back handler stack, cancellable `shop:native-back` event fallback, and conservative Ant Design modal/drawer close-button fallback. `NativeBackNavigation` now calls `consumeNativeBack()` before route, home, minimize, or exit handling. The native update modal registers a handler that consumes mandatory update prompts and dismisses optional prompts; cart drawer, product list filter drawer, quick-add and preview modals, product detail image and size-guide modals, support panel/order select, and support order-detail modal now register native Back handlers that close/consume before navigation.

### F570: Android release final publish can leave download directories split after a late destination failure

- Status: FIXED
- Area: Android App release publishing / multi-destination rollback
- Environment: `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/scripts/build-android-apk.js`, `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/public/downloads`, `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/build/downloads`, `/var/www/shoptest/downloads`, release-signed Android `npm run build:apk` final publish path
- Steps: Static review the release-signed final publish flow after F568/F569. Follow `publishReleaseStage(stage)` and the outer rollback block when public release signing is configured, then consider a late failure while copying to `frontend/build/downloads`, `/var/www/shoptest/downloads`, or during retired APK cleanup after an earlier directory was already updated.
- Expected: Final APK/manifest publication should be all-or-rollback across every customer-facing download directory. If any destination copy, rename, permission change, or cleanup step fails, previously updated public/build/live directories should be restored to their prior APK/manifest state or the release should remain unpublished everywhere.
- Actual: `publishReleaseStage(stage)` publishes generated release source, then calls `publishReleaseDirectory(...)` for `frontend/public/downloads`, optionally `frontend/build/downloads`, and then the Nginx download directory in sequence. `publishReleaseDirectory(...)` uses per-file temp rename, but it does not snapshot the old `shoptest.apk`, versioned APK, `mobile-version.json`, or retired APK list for rollback. If a later destination or cleanup fails after an earlier directory has received the new APK/manifest, the catch path rolls back the Gradle fallback version and restores/removes `frontend/src/generated/mobileRelease.ts` only when `finalReleasePublished` is still false; it does not undo files already copied into public/build/Nginx download directories.
- Evidence: Static source/download-directory review only. `build-android-apk.js` lines 491-497 copies the versioned APK, stable APK, manifest, then cleans retired APKs for one directory. Lines 500-510 publish public, build, and Nginx directories sequentially. Lines 548-554 roll back Gradle metadata if final publish throws, and lines 557-560 restore generated source when `finalReleasePublished` is false, but there is no target-directory snapshot or rollback of published APK/manifest files. Current inspected download directories contain only `mobile-version.json`, so this is a release-pipeline risk rather than a current public APK exposure. No release script, build, Gradle task, APK inspection, automated test, emulator, UI smoke, screenshot, video, source change, or commit was run.
- Impact: A disk, permission, ownership, or cleanup failure in one destination can create a split Android release: for example `frontend/public/downloads` advertises a new APK/manifest while `/var/www/shoptest/downloads` remains old, or newly copied APKs remain after `build.gradle` and generated release source were rolled back. This weakens release auditability, can make storefront/native update metadata differ by served directory, and can require manual cleanup during a failed production publish.
- Suggested fix: Treat final publication as a transaction across all destinations: snapshot existing target files and retired APKs, publish to temporary filenames/directories, validate every destination, then commit all targets or restore prior files on any failure. At minimum, track files copied/removed per destination and delete/restore them in the catch path before rolling back version/source metadata.
- Severity: Medium
- Resolution: `build-android-apk.js` now deduplicates final release download targets and snapshots each destination before copying any final APK/manifest files. The snapshot includes `shoptest.apk`, `mobile-version.json`, the new versioned APK name, and all existing versioned APKs that cleanup may retire. If any destination publish or cleanup step fails, the script restores the snapshotted release files in reverse target order and removes files/directories that did not exist before the failed publish, then rethrows so the existing Gradle version and generated release-source rollback still run.

### F569: Android release script can leave generated mobileRelease.ts pointing at an unpublished APK after second-pass failure

- Status: FIXED
- Area: Android App release quality / generated release metadata rollback
- Environment: `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/scripts/build-android-apk.js`, `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/generated/mobileRelease.ts`, Android release-signed `npm run build:apk` two-pass packaging flow
- Steps: Static review the release-signed Android packaging flow after the first APK assemble. Follow `prepareReleaseStage()`, `publishGeneratedReleaseSource()`, the second `syncAndroid()` / `assembleAndroidApk()`, and the final publish/rollback block.
- Expected: Generated release source should only be left in the working tree after the final APK and matching public/build/live manifests are successfully published, or it should be restored if any later release gate fails. A failed second WebView sync, stale-asset guard, Gradle assemble, APK certificate check, or final publish should not leave `src/generated/mobileRelease.ts` advertising an APK that was never released.
- Actual: After the first `syncAndroid()` and `assembleAndroidApk()`, the script stages a manifest from the first APK and immediately calls `publishGeneratedReleaseSource(stage)` before the second WebView sync and second APK assemble. If the second `syncAndroid()` or `assembleAndroidApk()` fails, execution stops before final `publishReleaseStage(...)`, but there is no `try/catch` or restore path for the already-written `frontend/src/generated/mobileRelease.ts`. The only explicit rollback in this section restores the Gradle version fallback after final publish failure; it does not restore the generated release source written before the second pass.
- Evidence: Static source review only. `build-android-apk.js` lines 470-472 copy the staged generated release source to `frontend/src/generated/mobileRelease.ts`. Lines 514-516 do that before lines 518-520 run the second WebView sync and assemble. Lines 527-532 only wrap `androidVersionBump.persist()` plus final `publishReleaseStage(stage)` and roll back Gradle metadata, not `mobileRelease.ts`. Current `frontend/src/generated/mobileRelease.ts` is a generated file consumed by `mobileUpdate.ts` for current release identity and app-id validation. No npm build, Gradle task, Maven/Jest, emulator, UI smoke, screenshot, video, source change, or commit was run.
- Impact: A failed second-pass release attempt can leave source metadata for an APK that was never finally packaged/published. Later frontend or native WebView builds can embed misleading current-version/app-id release identity, release auditors can see generated metadata drift from public `mobile-version.json`, and retry behavior becomes harder to reason about alongside F562 stale-asset recovery.
- Suggested fix: Snapshot `frontend/src/generated/mobileRelease.ts` before the pre-second-pass publish and restore it if any later `syncAndroid()`, `assembleAndroidApk()`, certificate verification, or final publish step fails. Alternatively, write the generated release source to a temporary location for the second WebView build and only persist it to source during the same final transaction as APK/manifest publish.
- Severity: Medium
- Resolution: `build-android-apk.js` now snapshots `frontend/src/generated/mobileRelease.ts` before publishing the staged first-pass release source for the second WebView build. If the second `syncAndroid()`, `assembleAndroidApk()`, certificate verification, or final publish transaction fails before `finalReleasePublished=true`, the script restores the previous generated source content or removes the generated file if it did not previously exist. Successful final publish still writes the final staged generated source alongside APK and manifest publication.

### F568: Android WebView release build is blocked when public downloads contain no versioned APK

- Status: FIXED
- Area: Android App release quality / WebView asset build bootstrap
- Environment: `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/package.json`, `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/scripts/build-web.js`, `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/scripts/build-android-apk.js`, `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/package.json`, `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/scripts/generate-mobile-version.js`, current `frontend/public/downloads`, `frontend/build/downloads`, and `/var/www/shoptest/downloads`
- Steps: Static review the Android native `npm run build:apk` and `npm run sync:android` path from the mobile shell. Follow `build-android-apk.js` into `syncAndroid()`, then the `sync:android` package script into `build:web`, then `build-web.js` into the frontend `npm run build` lifecycle. Compare that lifecycle with the current contents of the public/build/live download directories.
- Expected: A clean Android native release/sync should be able to build WebView assets before an APK exists in public downloads. Release metadata for the APK being built should either be staged after Gradle produces the APK, or the prebuild step should tolerate the signed-release bootstrap state without requiring an already-published versioned APK.
- Actual: The Android release script calls `syncAndroid()` before `assembleAndroidApk()`. `syncAndroid()` runs `npm run sync:android`, whose first step is `npm run build:web`; `build-web.js` runs `npm run build` inside the frontend. The frontend `prebuild` lifecycle runs `scripts/generate-mobile-version.js`, and that script throws when it cannot find a `shoptest-x.y.z.apk` in `frontend/public/downloads`. Current `frontend/public/downloads`, `frontend/build/downloads`, and `/var/www/shoptest/downloads` contain only `mobile-version.json` and no `shoptest.apk` or versioned APK files, so the native WebView build path can fail before generating assets or assembling the new APK.
- Evidence: Static source/config/download-directory review only. `shoptest-mobile/package.json` routes `sync:android` through `npm run build:web`; `scripts/build-web.js` lines 4-10 runs frontend `npm run build`; frontend `package.json` lines 24-28 defines `prebuild: node scripts/generate-mobile-version.js`; `generate-mobile-version.js` lines 101-110 selects versioned APKs from `public/downloads` and throws `No versioned APK matching ...` when none are present. `build-android-apk.js` lines 397-400 performs `syncAndroid()` before lines 505-506 assemble an APK, while its later staged `MOBILE_APK_PATH` flow is only reached after an APK already exists. Static directory inspection found only `mobile-version.json` in the three download directories and no `shoptest.apk` / `shoptest-*.apk`. No npm build, Gradle task, Maven/Jest, emulator, UI smoke, screenshot, video, source change, or commit was run.
- Impact: After the recent debug/public APK cleanup, a developer with proper release signing can still be unable to produce the next Android App package from a clean download directory because the WebView build requires a previous public APK artifact. This blocks release-signed APK generation and WebView asset refresh, including the allowed rebuild/sync needed to close F562.
- Suggested fix: Decouple frontend `prebuild` release metadata generation from native WebView asset builds, or let mobile `build:web` pass explicit bootstrap metadata / skip public-download APK discovery until after Gradle has produced the staged APK. Add a static guard in `build-android-apk.js` that detects this no-versioned-APK bootstrap state before invoking frontend `npm run build` and routes to the staged release metadata flow.
- Severity: High
- Resolution: `generate-mobile-version.js` now keeps the normal public-download APK discovery strict by default, but supports explicit `MOBILE_RELEASE_ALLOW_EMPTY_APK=true` bootstrap output that writes a safe no-download manifest with blank APK URL/file/hash/certificate fields and `releaseSigned=false`. The mobile shell `build-web.js` supplies Android version metadata and that bootstrap flag for native WebView builds when no staged APK is supplied, so `sync:android` can build assets from a clean downloads directory. During the release script's second WebView rebuild, `build-android-apk.js` passes `MOBILE_RELEASE_SKIP_GENERATION=true` after publishing the staged release source, preventing the frontend `prebuild` lifecycle from overwriting staged APK metadata before the final signed APK is assembled and published.

### F567: Mobile WebView runtime-config version injection no longer parses the env-backed Gradle version format

- Status: FIXED
- Area: Android App release quality / packaged WebView version metadata
- Environment: `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/scripts/prepare-web-assets.js`, `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/android/app/build.gradle`, Android `npm run sync:android` / `npm run build:apk` WebView asset preparation flow
- Steps: Static review how the mobile shell prepares `web/runtime-config.js` before Capacitor sync. Compare `prepare-web-assets.js`'s `readAndroidVersion()` parser with the current `android/app/build.gradle` version declarations introduced by the F564 release-version staging fix.
- Expected: WebView asset preparation should read the actual native Android version metadata used for the package, including the `SHOPTEST_MOBILE_ANDROID_VERSION_CODE` / `SHOPTEST_MOBILE_ANDROID_VERSION_NAME` environment values passed by the release script, or at minimum parse the current Gradle fallback expression. Generated runtime config should not write blank `mobileCurrentVersionName` or `mobileCurrentVersionCode: 0`.
- Actual: `prepare-web-assets.js` still searches for literal `versionName "..."` and `versionCode <digits>` lines. Current `build.gradle` now uses `versionCode mobileVersionCode ? mobileVersionCode.toInteger() : 23` and `versionName mobileVersionName ?: "1.0.23"`, so both old regexes fail. A regenerated `runtime-config.js` from the current scripts can therefore carry `mobileCurrentVersionName: ""` and `mobileCurrentVersionCode: 0` even when Gradle is packaging a specific app version through environment variables.
- Evidence: Static source/config review only. `prepare-web-assets.js` lines 152-162 read Gradle with `/versionName\s+"([^"]+)"/` and `/versionCode\s+(\d+)/`, then lines 180-218 write those parsed values into `window.__SHOP_RUNTIME_CONFIG__`. `android/app/build.gradle` lines 17-28 define `mobileVersionCode` / `mobileVersionName` env/property values and use conditional fallback expressions instead of literal version lines. A read-only Node regex check against the current Gradle file returned `versionNameRegexMatch=false` and `versionCodeRegexMatch=false`. No npm build, Gradle task, generated asset sync, automated test, emulator, UI smoke, screenshot, video, trace, source change, or commit was run.
- Impact: Native users and release auditors can receive WebView runtime metadata that does not match the APK actually built. In update flows this weakens installed-version comparisons and user-facing update copy, especially if generated release source is stale or a debug/internal sync is used; in release QA it also makes packaged assets harder to verify against the APK version.
- Suggested fix: Make `prepare-web-assets.js` prefer `SHOPTEST_MOBILE_ANDROID_VERSION_NAME` / `SHOPTEST_MOBILE_ANDROID_VERSION_CODE` from the environment, then parse the current Gradle fallback expressions if env values are absent. Add a static guard that fails WebView asset preparation when the generated runtime config would contain blank or zero mobile version metadata for Android packaging.
- Severity: Medium
- Retest: 2026-06-01 23:23 UTC static source review confirmed `prepare-web-assets.js` now prefers `SHOPTEST_MOBILE_ANDROID_VERSION_NAME` / `SHOPTEST_MOBILE_ANDROID_VERSION_CODE`, parses the current `versionCode mobileVersionCode ? mobileVersionCode.toInteger() : 23` and `versionName mobileVersionName ?: "1.0.23"` fallback expressions, and throws if Android runtime version metadata would be blank or zero. `node --check scripts/prepare-web-assets.js`, a targeted Node regex check against the current Gradle fallback, and an env-version guard source scan passed. No npm build, Gradle task, generated asset sync, automated test, emulator, UI smoke, screenshot, video, trace, or commit was run per instruction.

### F566: Android hardware Back is swallowed on the native App root route

- Status: FIXED
- Area: Android native shell UI / hardware navigation
- Environment: `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/App.tsx`, Android Capacitor App plugin, packaged WebView `main.52f37fa4.js`
- Steps: Static review the Android native back-button listener used by the WebView shell. Start from `NativeBackNavigation` in `App.tsx` and compare its root-route behavior with the Capacitor App plugin's documented `backButton` behavior.
- Expected: On Android, pressing hardware Back should navigate back within the app when route history exists; when navigation is complete at the root route, it should either close/minimize the native app through `App.exitApp()`/`minimizeApp()` or intentionally delegate to Android's default behavior. The app should not silently ignore the hardware Back action at `/`.
- Actual: `NativeBackNavigation` always registers an `App.addListener('backButton', ...)` listener in native mode. The handler calls `navigate(-1)` when its internal route stack has more than one entry, or `navigate('/', { replace: true })` when the current path is not `/`. When the app is already at `/` with no route stack, the handler does nothing and never calls `App.exitApp()` or `minimizeApp()`. Capacitor documents that listening for `backButton` disables the default back behavior and that closing the app requires `App.exitApp()`.
- Evidence: Static source/generated-asset review only. `App.tsx` lines 386-405 registers the `backButton` listener and lines 394-403 contain no root-route exit/minimize/default branch. A targeted source scan found `backButton` registration but no `exitApp(` or `minimizeApp(` usage in the frontend. The packaged Android WebView `main.52f37fa4.js` also contains the same minified listener branch without an exit call. Local `@capacitor/app` README lines 368-376 state that listening for `backButton` disables default behavior and says to call `App.exitApp()` to close the app. No emulator, runtime UI smoke, screenshot, video, trace, build, automated test, source change, or commit was run.
- Impact: Android users who press Back from the home/root screen can see no response, which feels broken and prevents the standard Android escape path from the native shell. This affects the first-screen/home path and every flow that navigates back to `/`, including product browsing, cart/checkout return, login/register, support, and profile workflows.
- Suggested fix: Add an explicit root-route branch for Android native back handling, for example `App.exitApp()` or `minimizeApp()` after confirming no modal/drawer should consume Back. Alternatively disable the custom back-button handler when the app wants Capacitor/Android default behavior. Add a small static/unit-level guard around root-route back handling when tests are allowed.
- Severity: Medium
- Retest: 2026-06-01 23:23 UTC static source review confirmed `App.tsx` now keeps `navigate(-1)` for internal native route stack back, navigates non-root paths to `/`, and explicitly calls `App.minimizeApp()` at root when available, falling back to `App.exitApp()`. Targeted source scans found the `backButton` listener plus `minimizeApp`/`exitApp` branches. No frontend build, generated WebView asset sync, automated test, emulator, UI smoke, screenshot, video, trace, or commit was run per instruction.

### F565: Native update download path depends on an unregistered Browser plugin

- Status: FIXED
- Area: Android App update/download flow / native shell plugin packaging
- Environment: `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/utils/mobileUpdate.ts`, `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/package.json`, `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/android/app/src/main/assets/capacitor.plugins.json`, `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/android/app/src/main/java/com/shoptest/mobile/MainActivity.java`

- Expected: When the native App shows a signed update prompt, tapping Download should use a packaged native external-browser/download mechanism, or the Android shell should provide an explicit WebView download/intent handler. The required plugin/handler should be present in the packaged native app before a release APK is published.
- Actual: `openMobileReleaseDownload(...)` first tries `window.Capacitor?.Plugins?.Browser.open({ url })`, but `shoptest-mobile/package.json` depends only on `@capacitor/android`, `@capacitor/app`, `@capacitor/core`, and `@capacitor/ios`; generated `capacitor.plugins.json` registers only `@capacitor/app`; and `MainActivity` is an empty `BridgeActivity` with no custom `DownloadListener` or external `Intent` handling. If `Browser` is absent, the code falls back to `window.open(url, '_system', ...)` and then `window.location.assign(url)` in the WebView.
