No release-signed manifest was injected, and no npm build, Gradle task, emulator, UI smoke, APK inspection, screenshot, video, trace, source change, or commit was run in this QA pass.
- Impact: Once a real release-signed update is published, the native update modal can present a Download action whose preferred native external-browser path is unavailable in the packaged app. Depending on WebView behavior, the tap may do nothing, open an in-WebView APK URL, or replace the storefront shell with a download response instead of handing off cleanly to Android's browser/package installer flow.
- Suggested fix: Add and sync `@capacitor/browser` (or another explicit native external-open/download mechanism) for the mobile shell and verify it appears in generated plugin metadata before release packaging. Alternatively, implement a native Android download/intent handler for release APK URLs and add a static packaging check that fails when `openMobileReleaseDownload` references `Browser` but the plugin/handler is absent.
- Severity: Medium
- Retest: 2026-06-01 23:15 UTC static source/config review confirmed `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/package.json` and `package-lock.json` now include `@capacitor/browser` 7.x, `node_modules/@capacitor/browser` is installed with scripts ignored, Android `capacitor.settings.gradle` includes `:capacitor-browser`, Android `app/capacitor.build.gradle` depends on `project(':capacitor-browser')`, and `android/app/src/main/assets/capacitor.plugins.json` registers `com.capacitorjs.plugins.browser.BrowserPlugin`. `build-android-apk.js` now verifies those registrations after `sync:android` whenever the storefront update-download source references `Plugins?.Browser`. `node --check scripts/build-android-apk.js`, package/plugin JSON parsing, and targeted dependency/registration scans passed. No `cap sync`, npm build, Gradle task, Maven/Jest, emulator, UI smoke, APK inspection, screenshot, generated WebView sync, or commit was run per instruction.

### F564: Android release script leaves version bump behind when packaging fails

- Status: FIXED
- Area: Android App release quality / version metadata integrity
- Environment: `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/scripts/build-android-apk.js`, `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/android/app/build.gradle`, Android `npm run build:apk` release-signed path
- Steps: Static review the release-signed APK publish path. Follow the order from release-signing validation through `bumpAndroidVersion()`, `syncAndroid()`, `assembleAndroidApk()`, staging, and final publish.
- Expected: Android versionCode/versionName changes should be committed only after the release build has passed WebView asset verification, Gradle packaging, APK certificate verification, staged manifest generation, and final public publish, or the script should roll back the version file on any later failure.
- Actual: After release signing is configured, `build-android-apk.js` calls `bumpAndroidVersion()` immediately and writes `android/app/build.gradle` in place before the first `syncAndroid()` and `assembleAndroidApk()`. Any later failure in `npm run sync:android`, the F562 stale-asset guard, Gradle assemble, APK certificate verification, staging, second sync/build, or final publish leaves the bumped `versionCode`/`versionName` in the working tree even though no matching APK/manifest may have been published.
- Evidence: Static source review only. `bumpAndroidVersion()` writes `android/app/build.gradle` at lines 253-275; the release path calls it at line 307 before `syncAndroid()` and `assembleAndroidApk()` at lines 427-428 and before the second sync/build at lines 440-442. No rollback/finally path restores the original Gradle file. Current checked Gradle metadata is `versionCode 23` / `versionName "1.0.23"`, and public/build/live download directories still contain only unsigned/empty `mobile-version.json` files. No release script, Gradle task, npm build, automated test, emulator, UI smoke, screenshot, video, trace, source change, or commit was run in this QA pass.
- Impact: A failed release attempt can consume or drift Android version numbers without producing a matching public release. Repeated failures can desynchronize `build.gradle`, `mobile-version.json`, generated WebView runtime config, and operator expectations, making rollback/retry audits harder and increasing the chance of shipping the wrong version metadata later.
- Suggested fix: Stage the next Android version metadata in memory or a temporary Gradle copy until all release gates pass, then atomically persist `build.gradle` with the APK/manifest publish. Alternatively, wrap the release path in a try/catch that restores the original Gradle file unless final publish succeeds, and add a static/release check covering failure rollback.
- Severity: Medium
- Retest: 2026-06-01 23:12 UTC static source review confirmed `build-android-apk.js` no longer calls or writes an immediate `bumpAndroidVersion()` before the first `syncAndroid()`/`assembleAndroidApk()`. The script now computes the next version with `createAndroidVersionBump()`, passes it to Gradle via `SHOPTEST_MOBILE_ANDROID_VERSION_CODE` / `SHOPTEST_MOBILE_ANDROID_VERSION_NAME`, and only persists the checked `build.gradle` fallback during final publish with rollback on publish failure. `android/app/build.gradle` now uses those temporary environment values for packaging while keeping `versionCode 23` / `versionName "1.0.23"` as the current fallback. `node --check scripts/build-android-apk.js`, a targeted Node regex check against the current Gradle fallback, and source scans for the version/publish flow passed. No npm build, Gradle task, Maven/Jest, emulator, UI smoke, APK inspection, generated asset sync, or commit was run per instruction.

### F563: Android WebView asset build allows TypeScript compile errors to ship

- Status: FIXED
- Area: Android App release quality / packaged WebView build gate
- Environment: `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/scripts/build-web.js`, `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/package.json`, `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/package.json`, Android `npm run build:apk` / `npm run sync:android` flow
- Steps: Static review the Android native shell web build wrapper and package scripts used before Capacitor sync/package. Compare the mobile wrapper environment with the normal frontend production build script.
- Expected: Android App WebView assets should be built with the same or stricter compile gate as the storefront production build. TypeScript compile errors should fail `npm run build:web`, stop `prepare:web`, stop `cap sync android`, and prevent APK packaging/publishing.
- Actual: `scripts/build-web.js` runs `npm run build` in the frontend with `TSC_COMPILE_ON_ERROR: 'true'` injected into the environment. The mobile `sync`, `sync:android`, `sync:ios`, and `build:apk` flows all call this wrapper before preparing/syncing WebView assets. The frontend `package.json` production build itself does not set this override, but the Android native packaging wrapper does, so a TypeScript-broken storefront can still emit bundled JS for the native shell.
- Evidence: Static source review only. `build-web.js` lines 5-10 sets `TSC_COMPILE_ON_ERROR: 'true'`; `package.json` lines 9-12 route native sync/APK flows through `npm run build:web`; frontend `package.json` line 27 uses `GENERATE_SOURCEMAP=false react-scripts build` without that override. No TypeScript error was injected, and no `npm build`, Gradle, Jest, Maven, emulator, UI smoke, screenshot, video, trace, source change, or commit was run in this QA pass.
- Impact: A future TypeScript regression in login/register/cart/checkout/profile/support/update-flow code can be silently bundled into the Android WebView shell and then pass the later static asset guard if the generated JS lacks the specific stale-release patterns. This weakens release quality for core mobile user paths and can produce APKs from code the normal production build would reject.
- Suggested fix: Remove `TSC_COMPILE_ON_ERROR=true` from the mobile build wrapper, or restrict it to an explicit non-release local debug mode that cannot feed `prepare:web`, `sync:android`, or `build:apk`. Add a static release check that fails when release packaging scripts set `TSC_COMPILE_ON_ERROR=true`.
- Severity: Medium
- Retest: 2026-06-01 23:03 UTC static source review confirmed `scripts/build-web.js` now passes `TSC_COMPILE_ON_ERROR=false` into the frontend production build wrapper, and targeted scans found no `TSC_COMPILE_ON_ERROR=true` / `COMPILE_ON_ERROR=true` setting in the mobile shell scripts, package scripts, frontend build script, or frontend scripts. `node --check scripts/build-web.js` passed. No TypeScript error was injected, and no `npm build`, Gradle, Jest, Maven, emulator, UI smoke, screenshot, video, trace, or commit was run per instruction.

### F559: Native update flow accepts signed manifests without explicit APK artifact metadata

- Status: FIXED
- Area: Android App release quality / native update prompt and download metadata
- Environment: `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/src/utils/mobileUpdate.ts`, native App update gate, storefront Android download resolver, `/downloads/mobile-version.json`
- Steps: Static review the release-manifest normalizer and download resolver. Consider a future manifest with the expected Android platform/app id, positive `versionCode`, `releaseSigned: true`, and a valid non-debug `certificateSha256`, but missing or blank `apkUrl`, `fileName`, `sizeBytes`, and `sha256`.
- Expected: A production native update/download surface should fail closed unless the release manifest explicitly names the APK artifact and includes immutable artifact metadata such as positive size and a 64-character APK SHA-256. It should not guess a downloadable APK URL when the signed release manifest is incomplete.
- Actual: `normalizeReleaseManifest(...)` derives `apkUrl` from `source.apkUrl || buildVersionedAndroidApkUrl(versionName) || legacyApkUrl`, while `isMobileReleaseDownloadAllowed(...)` only requires `releaseSigned === true` and a valid non-debug certificate fingerprint. `resolveMobileReleaseDownloadUrl(...)` repeats the same fallback to `/downloads/shoptest-{versionName}.apk` or the legacy APK URL. A signed-but-incomplete manifest can therefore still drive the update prompt/download URL even though no artifact URL/hash/size was explicitly published. Current deployed manifests are unsigned, so this is not prompting users today.
- Evidence: Static source review only: `mobileUpdate.ts` lines 213-226 and 244-260. No manifest mutation, runtime App check, build, automated test, screenshot, video, trace, or source change was run in this QA pass.
- Impact: A release metadata mistake can send Android App users to a stale, missing, or mismatched APK path without a manifest-level SHA/size guard. This weakens the release/download quality gate even after F334/F422 certificate gating.
- Suggested fix: For release-signed manifests, require explicit `apkUrl`, `fileName`, positive `sizeBytes`, and a normalized 64-character APK `sha256` before allowing any native update or storefront download link. Remove guessed APK URL fallback for production release manifests, or limit it to clearly separated local debug/dev mode.
- Severity: Medium
- Retest: 2026-06-01 22:44 UTC static source review confirmed `isMobileReleaseDownloadAllowed(...)` now requires `releaseSigned=true`, a valid non-debug release certificate fingerprint, safe explicit `apkUrl`, safe APK `fileName`, positive `sizeBytes`, and a normalized 64-character APK `sha256`. `resolveMobileReleaseDownloadUrl(...)` now uses only the explicit manifest `apkUrl` after that gate and no longer guesses a versioned or legacy APK URL for signed releases; `normalizeReleaseManifest(...)` no longer synthesizes `apkUrl` from the version. No manifest mutation, runtime App check, build, automated test, screenshot, video, trace, or commit was run per instruction.

### F558: Android Cordova allowlist permits all origins in the packaged native shell

- Status: FIXED
- Area: Android App WebView/Cordova security configuration
- Environment: `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/android/app/src/main/res/xml/config.xml`, `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/android/app/build.gradle`, bundled `assets/public/runtime-config.js`
- Steps: Static review the Capacitor/Cordova Android shell configuration and compare the WebView allowlist with the production runtime endpoints.
- Expected: A commercial WebView-like Android App should restrict Cordova/WebView access to the required production HTTPS/WSS origins, with localhost/debug allowances kept in debug-only configuration if needed.
- Actual: `config.xml` contains `<access origin="*" />` while the Android app includes `project(':capacitor-cordova-android-plugins')` and the bundled runtime endpoints are fixed to `https://pet.686888666.xyz/api` and `wss://pet.686888666.xyz/ws/support`. The native shell therefore keeps a broad Cordova origin allowlist that is wider than the production app requires.
- Evidence: Static source review only: `config.xml` line 3, `android/app/build.gradle` line 70, and bundled `runtime-config.js` lines 32-55. No runtime navigation attempt, emulator, build, automated test, screenshot, video, trace, or source change was run in this QA pass.
- Impact: If any current or future Cordova/Capacitor plugin, navigation, or network bridge consults the Cordova allowlist, the packaged App can permit arbitrary origins rather than only the intended shop backend/origin. This increases blast radius if WebView content is redirected or injected.
- Suggested fix: Replace the wildcard with explicit production origins required by the App, and keep any local development origins in a debug-only config. Add a static release check that fails packaging when production `config.xml` contains `<access origin="*" />`.
- Severity: Medium
- Retest: 2026-06-01 22:44 UTC static source review confirmed Android and iOS Cordova `config.xml` now use `<access origin="https://pet.686888666.xyz" />` and no checked native mobile config contains `<access origin="*" />`. No runtime navigation attempt, emulator, Gradle build, automated test, screenshot, video, trace, or commit was run per instruction.

### F557: Android APK publish script copies public APKs before release manifest validation completes

- Status: FIXED
- Area: Android App release publishing / update manifest integrity
- Environment: `/home/guhao/shoptest-mobile/scripts/build-android-apk.js`, `/home/guhao/shoptest/frontend/scripts/generate-mobile-version.js`, `frontend/public/downloads`, `frontend/build/downloads`, `/var/www/shoptest/downloads`
- Steps: Static review the Android APK release publish script and manifest generator order after the F556 debug-publish fix.
- Expected: The release pipeline should validate signing metadata, APK version metadata, SHA/size metadata, and manifest generation before copying any APK into public or live download directories. Publishing APK plus `mobile-version.json` should be staged and atomic, and old APK cleanup should happen only after the new manifest/artifact pair is ready.
- Actual: In the release-signed path, after `syncAndroid()` and `assembleAndroidApk()`, the script still calls `publishApkArtifacts()` before `publishMobileVersionManifest()`. `publishApkArtifacts()` copies `shoptest.apk` and the versioned APK into public/build/live download directories and removes retired APKs. Only after that does `publishMobileVersionManifest()` run `generate-mobile-version.js`, which can still fail on version/signing/update-policy metadata. A post-copy manifest failure can leave a public APK without the matching trusted manifest/checksum metadata, and can remove the previous versioned APK before the new release is fully valid.
- Evidence: Static source review only: `build-android-apk.js` lines 213-239 and 285-292, plus `generate-mobile-version.js` lines 23-34, 58-69, 87-102, and 104-124. Current download directories were inspected and contain only `mobile-version.json`, no APK files, so the issue is a release-pipeline risk rather than current public APK exposure. No build, release script, automated test, screenshot, video, trace, or source change was run in this QA pass.
- Impact: A failed release publish can create a partial public Android release in `frontend/public`, `frontend/build`, or `/var/www`, causing stale/discoverable APK files, missing or mismatched update metadata, and a harder rollback path.
- Suggested fix: Stage the APK in a temporary/private directory, validate/generate the manifest against the staged artifact, then atomically publish the APK and manifest together. Defer retired-APK cleanup until after manifest publish succeeds, and clean up newly copied artifacts if any post-copy step fails.
- Severity: Medium
- Retest: 2026-06-01 22:44 UTC static source review confirmed the release script now stages `shoptest.apk` and the versioned APK under `.release-staging`, runs `generate-mobile-version.js` against the staged versioned APK through `MOBILE_APK_PATH`/`MOBILE_APK_FILE_NAME` and staged output paths, publishes `mobileRelease.ts` before the second packaging pass, and only copies the final staged APKs plus `mobile-version.json` to public/build/live download directories after final manifest generation succeeds. Public copies use temp-file rename, retired APK cleanup runs after per-directory publish, and staging directories are removed on success or staging failure. `node --check` passed for both release scripts; no release build, Gradle task, artifact inspection, automated test, screenshot, video, trace, or commit was run per instruction.

- Status: FIXED
- Area: Mobile App / update manifest and APK download URL handling
- Environment: `frontend/src/utils/mobileUpdate.ts`, native App update prompt, Navbar Android download entry, runtime-configured mobile manifest URL, and `frontend/public/downloads/mobile-version.json`

- Expected: Commercial App update/download code should only open a trusted HTTPS URL, a local-development HTTP URL, or a safe relative asset resolved from a trusted origin. Malformed or attacker-controlled URL shapes should be rejected before reaching `window.open`, the Capacitor Browser plugin, or a visible download link.
- Actual: The resolver previously normalized strings by trimming control characters and then passed more URL shapes through origin resolution. That left the update/download path too permissive for manifest-provided values that should never be accepted in a production mobile update surface.
- Evidence: Parallel App worker static review at 2026-06-01 06:20 UTC inspected the mobile update chain in `mobileUpdate.ts`, `App.tsx`, `Navbar.tsx`, runtime config, and the current public mobile manifest. The review identified the unsafe URL-shape gap as distinct from F334's debug-signing release issue.
- Retest: 2026-06-01 06:22 UTC static source review confirmed `normalizeMobileUrlValue(...)`, `parseSafeMobileHttpUrl(...)`, and `resolveMobileAssetUrl(...)` now reject control characters, backslashes, `%00`, `%5c`, protocol-relative URLs, URL credentials, non-HTTP(S) schemes, and non-localhost plaintext HTTP remote origins while preserving HTTPS, localhost HTTP, and safe relative-path resolution. No build, automated test, UI smoke, screenshot, or commit was run per instruction.
- Expected fix direction: Keep the URL allowlist strict and add regression tests around release-manifest URL normalization when tests are allowed. F334 separately requires a release-signed APK and publishing workflow.

### F341: GET payment history/latest endpoints mutate payment and order state

- Status: FIXED
- Evidence: 2026-05-30 23:34 UTC static review found `PaymentController.java` lines 201-235 expose authenticated and guest payment history/latest GET routes under both class-level mappings (`/payments` and `/payment`) and delegate to `PaymentService.findByOrderId()` or `PaymentService.findLatestByOrderId()`. `PaymentService.java` lines 272-290 and 314-325 call `syncProviderPaymentState(...)` and `expirePayment(...)` inside those read helpers. `expirePayment()` at lines 377-385 calls `paymentRepository.markExpired(...)` and can call `orderService.cancelOrder(...)` when no active pending payment remains; `syncProviderPaymentState()` at lines 637-669 retrieves Stripe sessions, can call `paymentRepository.markPaidDetailed(...)`, and can move the order to `PENDING_SHIPMENT`.

The state-changing `findByOrderId(...)` / `findLatestByOrderId(...)` methods remain available for explicit sync/expiry workflows but are no longer used by GET history/latest reads. No build, automated test, screenshot, video, or trace was run in this pass.
- Expected fix direction: Split side-effect-free payment history/latest reads from state-changing sync/expiry workflows. Keep GET endpoints on read-only repository access, and invoke provider sync/expiry only from explicit sync endpoints, callbacks/webhooks, scheduled expiry jobs, or deliberate customer/admin actions with audit coverage.

### F339: Nginx cache-control locations drop inherited security headers

- Status: FIXED
- Evidence: 2026-05-30 23:17 UTC static review found `deploy/nginx/shoptest-static.conf` lines 61-66 and `deploy/nginx/shoptest-edge.conf.template` lines 63-68 declare HTTPS server-level security headers, including `X-Frame-Options`, `X-Content-Type-Options`, `Referrer-Policy`, `Permissions-Policy`, `Strict-Transport-Security`, and `Content-Security-Policy`. Child locations then define only `add_header Cache-Control` at `shoptest-static.conf` lines 68-70, 94-97, 101-103, 107-108, 112-114, 118-120, and 150-158, and at `shoptest-edge.conf.template` lines 70-72, 96-99, 103-105, 109-110, 114-116, 120-122, and 150-161. Because Nginx inherits parent `add_header` directives only when the child context has no `add_header` directives, representative `/healthz`, `/static/*`, denied `*.map`, `/runtime-config.js`, SPA fallback, generic asset, and `/uploads/` responses can lose the security headers while still returning cache headers.
- Retest: 2026-05-31 18:37 UTC static config review confirmed every HTTPS child location that declares `add_header Cache-Control` in `shoptest-static.conf` and `shoptest-edge.conf.template` now repeats `X-Frame-Options`, `X-Content-Type-Options`, `Referrer-Policy`, `Permissions-Policy`, `Strict-Transport-Security`, and `Content-Security-Policy`; HTTP `/healthz` repeats the core non-HSTS security headers. `git diff --check` passed for both Nginx files, and a text scan found no `Cache-Control` block missing the expected headers. No Nginx reload, live HTTP request, build, automated test, screenshot, video, or trace was run in this pass.
- Retest: 2026-05-31 18:44 UTC no-media curl/header regression against local Nginx was blocked by stale active config. The active `/etc/nginx/sites-enabled/shoptest` points to `/etc/nginx/sites-available/shoptest` modified `2026-05-30 02:32:59 +0000`, not the fixed repo deploy config. Curl via `--resolve pet.686888666.xyz` found HTTPS `/healthz`, `/static/css/main.24899161.css`, `/runtime-config.js`, `/favicon.ico`, denied `/static/js/main.6f32d2b3.js.map`, and `/uploads/f339-header-probe.jpg` returning Cache-Control but missing the full security header set; `/not-a-real-route` had security headers but missed Cache-Control. No Nginx reload/restart was performed, and no new product issue was added. 未截图、未录屏、未生成 trace/图片.
- Expected fix direction: Use a shared include/snippet or repeat the full security header set in every child location that declares `add_header`, or use a pinned supported Nginx inheritance mechanism. Verify representative static, runtime-config, denied-map, upload, health-check, and SPA fallback responses retain both cache and security headers.

### F338: Admin user status API can convert registered accounts into GUEST

- Status: FIXED
- Evidence: 2026-05-30 22:37 UTC static review found `AdminController.normalizeUserStatus()` accepts `GUEST` and `updateUser()` persists it for non-self, non-privileged customer rows. `UserManagement.tsx` locks only the visible action for rows already normalized to `GUEST`, so direct `PUT /admin/users/{customerId}` requests can still bypass the UI and mark a registered customer as a guest identity. `UserMapper.findActiveCustomerIds()` includes only `USER` rows with null/`ACTIVE` status, and `NotificationService.broadcastToCustomers()` uses that query for customer broadcasts.
- Expected fix direction: Treat `GUEST` as a system-owned guest-checkout status in the admin API: reject non-guest-to-guest transitions through `PUT /admin/users/{id}` unless a dedicated audited migration flow exists, and enforce the same guest-status lock server-side that the UI now presents.
- Evidence: Development handling at 2026-05-30 22:53 UTC added the backend guard in `AdminController.updateUser()`. Direct requests attempting to set `status=GUEST`, or to change an existing `GUEST` account through the admin status API, now return `Guest status is system-managed` before persistence.

### F217: Category deletion with assigned products falls through to database constraint errors

The admin and public category delete controllers catch only `IllegalArgumentException`, so database constraint failures from deleting a product-bearing leaf category can bypass the controlled 400/audit-failure path.

- Status: FIXED
- Evidence: Static verification found `UserManagement.tsx` disables the status toggle when `record.id === currentUserId`, but backend `AdminController.updateUser()` has no equivalent guard for `user.getStatus() != null`. The same controller blocks current-operator role changes and deletion, yet the status branch accepts `ACTIVE`, `BANNED`, or `GUEST`, assigns the normalized status, and persists it. `UserDetailsImpl.isEnabled()` returns false for `BANNED`, and `JwtAuthenticationFilter` only installs JWT authentication when the loaded user is enabled, so a direct backend request can self-ban the active operator account and lock out subsequent admin requests.
- Expected fix direction: Add a backend current-operator guard for status changes, returning an audited validation failure before persisting; consider limiting self-profile/admin updates to explicit fields so UI-disabled account controls cannot be bypassed by direct API calls.
- Evidence: Development handling at 2026-05-30 22:23 UTC added a backend self-status guard in `AdminController.updateUser()`. Direct `PUT /admin/users/{currentId}` status changes now return a controlled bad request and audit failure with `Cannot change current operator status`, matching the existing frontend disabled state and backend self-role/delete guards. No project tests/builds were run per instruction; static `git diff --check` and source grep were used.

### F208: Config center reloads masked secrets into the publish editor and blocks unrelated changes

- Status: FIXED
- Evidence: Static verification found `ConfigCenterService.buildResponse()` returns masked sensitive values in `content`, and `ConfigCenter.tsx` puts `response.data.content` directly into the editable `content` textarea. When the operator applies or publishes that editor text, `ConfigCenterService.validateParsedProperties(...)` rejects sensitive values containing `****`; existing tests separately verify response masking and rejection of `payment.callback-secret=su****90` placeholders. Any config file with an allowed secret key can therefore block an unrelated non-sensitive edit unless the operator re-enters/removes the secret.
- Expected fix direction: Keep masked secrets out of the editable publish payload, preserve unchanged secret keys server-side, or introduce an explicit placeholder protocol that resolves to the existing value instead of being parsed as a literal rejected value.
- Retest: 2026-05-31 21:25 UTC static source review found `ConfigCenterService.publishInternal(...)` calls `preserveMaskedSensitiveValues(...)` before validation. Masked sensitive keys are read from current Nacos content, raw current line values replace only matching masked placeholders, validation then runs against the restored content, and `buildResponse(...)` still masks sensitive content/properties/effective values before returning to the editor. `ConfigCenterServiceTest.preservesMaskedSensitivePlaceholderFromCurrentNacosContent()` covers the successful preserve/apply path, while `rejectsMaskedSensitivePlaceholderWhenOriginalValueCannotBeRead()` keeps the safe failure path. No build or automated test was run per instruction.

### F207: Admin user contact edits bypass customer email/phone validation and uniqueness checks

- Status: FIXED
- Evidence: Static verification found `UserManagement.tsx` sending admin profile edits through `adminApi.updateUser(...)` with only light frontend email/phone length checks. `AdminController.updateUser()` then assigns `email` and `phone` directly to the existing `User` and calls generic `userService.update(...)`, which only sets `updatedAt` and delegates to `UserMapper.update`. This bypasses `UserService.updateProfileContact(...)`, the validated contact path that lowercases/validates email, normalizes phone to the users column limit, and rejects duplicate email/phone ownership.
- Retest: 2026-05-31 20:14 UTC static source review found `UserService.update(...)` now loads the current row and calls `normalizeMutableProfileFields(...)` before persistence. That path lowercases and validates email, normalizes phone, limits address length, and rejects duplicate email/phone ownership through `findByUsernameOrPhoneOrEmail(...)` / `findByPhone(...)`. `AdminController.updateUser(...)` still routes profile edits through `userService.update(existing)`, so admin contact edits no longer bypass backend validation. No build or automated tests were run per instruction.
- Expected fix direction: Route admin contact edits through a shared validated contact-update service method, or add equivalent backend validation/normalization/duplicate checks and audited validation failures before calling the generic user update.

### F206: Payment provider/config failures can incorrectly escalate client IPs to the payment blacklist

- Status: FIXED
- Evidence: Static verification found `PaymentController` calls `ipBlacklistService.recordPaymentFailure(...)` for broad `IllegalArgumentException`/`IllegalStateException` failures across create, sync, simulation, generic callback, and Stripe webhook paths. `PaymentService` uses `IllegalStateException` for non-client faults such as missing Stripe/gateway configuration, provider request failures, invalid provider responses, disabled simulation, missing production callback secret, and missing Stripe webhook secret. Those failures flow into `IpBlacklistService.recordFailure(SOURCE_PAYMENT, ...)`, which blocks the caller IP after `security.ip-blacklist.payment-failure-threshold` failures.
- Expected fix direction: separate suspicious client-controlled payment failures from backend/provider outages before recording payment blacklist failures; keep outage/config failures in audit logs and system alerts without increasing blacklist counters.
- Retest: 2026-05-31 21:21 UTC static source review found `PaymentController.recordPaymentBlacklistFailureIfSuspicious(...)` now gates blacklist writes. `shouldRecordPaymentBlacklistFailure(...)` returns true for client-controlled `IllegalArgumentException` and 4xx `ResponseStatusException` failures only; provider/config/outage `IllegalStateException` paths such as missing Stripe/gateway settings, provider request/response failures, disabled simulation, and missing production callback secrets are audited but do not call `ipBlacklistService.recordPaymentFailure(...)`. Stripe webhook `IllegalStateException` is returned as `503` without blacklist escalation. No build or automated test was run per instruction.

### F205: Customer and guest confirm-receipt mutations bypass order audit logging

- Status: FIXED
- Evidence: Static verification at 2026-05-30 11:19 UTC found `OrderController.confirmReceipt()` and `confirmGuestReceipt()` both delegate to `confirmReceiptInternal()`, which validates registered-account or guest access, calls `orderService.updateOrderStatus(id, "COMPLETED")`, and returns `Order completed` without any `auditLogService.record(...)` call. `OrderService.assertNextStatus()` permits `SHIPPED -> COMPLETED`, and `updateOrderStatus()` writes the status plus customer notification. Nearby order lifecycle paths in the same controller record `ORDER_CANCEL`, `RETURN_REQUEST`, and `RETURN_SHIPMENT_SUBMIT`, and admin status updates record status-specific audit events, so customer/guest confirm receipt is the status-changing path missing audit coverage.
- Retest: 2026-05-31 20:14 UTC static source review found `OrderController.confirmReceiptInternal(...)` records `ORDER_CONFIRM_RECEIPT` success after `orderService.updateOrderStatus(id, "COMPLETED")`, and records failure in the catch block with order id, guest/auth context, previous status, order number, guest email, and guest order number metadata. No build or automated tests were run per instruction.
- Expected fix direction: Add success/failure audit logging for confirm receipt, including order id, actor or guest context, previous/next status, and order number; keep guest credential failures visible in the same audit family where feasible.

### F204: IP blacklist login-failure admin endpoint mutates blocks without audit logging

- Status: FIXED
- Evidence: Static verification at 2026-05-30 11:17 UTC found `AdminIpBlacklistController` auditing manual `IP_BLACKLIST_BLOCK`, `IP_BLACKLIST_RELEASE`, and `IP_BLACKLIST_BATCH_RELEASE`, but `@PostMapping("/record-login-failure")` only calls `ipBlacklistService.recordFailure(SOURCE_LOGIN, ...)` and returns 204. `IpBlacklistService.recordFailure()` inserts or updates `ip_blacklist_entries`, increments `failure_count`, can transition a row to `BLOCKED`, updates `blocked_at`/`blocked_until`, and emits a system alert via `recordBlockedAlert(...)`. Admin-triggered calls to that endpoint can therefore change blacklist state without the actor/request audit trail present on the other IP blacklist mutations.
- Retest: 2026-05-31 20:14 UTC static source review found `AdminIpBlacklistController.recordLoginFailure(...)` now requires `ip-blacklist:record-failure`, calls `ipBlacklistService.recordFailure(...)`, and records `IP_BLACKLIST_RECORD_LOGIN_FAILURE` success/failure audit events with masked IP/reason metadata. No build or automated tests were run per instruction.
- Expected fix direction: Either remove/lock down the endpoint if it is only a test/internal hook, or add the same success/failure audit coverage and actor/request metadata used by manual block and release operations.

### F203: User management exposes two role editors whose effects conflict for custom-role users

- Status: FIXED
- Evidence: Static verification at 2026-05-30 11:06 UTC found `UserManagement.tsx` rendering editable selects for both `roleCode` and legacy `role` on the same row. `handleRoleChange()` calls `adminApi.updateUser(userId, { role: newRole })`, while `handleRoleCodeChange()` calls `/admin/users/{id}/role-code`. Backend `AdminController.updateUser()` preserves `existing.getRoleCode()` whenever the new role is non-USER and the existing role code is nonblank; `AdminRoleService.getPermissionsForUser()` then prioritizes that nonblank role code over `role`. Changing a custom-role user through the legacy role dropdown can therefore leave effective permissions on the old custom role.
- Retest: 2026-05-31 20:14 UTC static source review found `UserManagement.tsx` now renders one editable role assignment control, the `roleCode` selector, and displays the legacy `role` column as a read-only tag. `handleRoleCodeChange(...)` routes `USER` to the standard role update and custom/admin role codes to `/admin/users/{id}/role-code`; backend standard role updates also map `ADMIN` and `SUPER_ADMIN` to their matching role codes instead of preserving stale custom codes. No build or automated tests were run per instruction.
- Expected fix direction: Remove the legacy role dropdown for role-code-managed users, route all role assignment through a single `roleCode` model, or clear/update `roleCode` explicitly when the UI assigns standard `ADMIN`/`USER` roles.

### F202: Order summary quick cards are counted with the active status filter but clicks clear that filter

- Status: FIXED

In `OrderManagement.tsx`, `handleQuickFilterChange()` sets `filterStatus(undefined)` and `syncRouteFilters({ quick: nextQuick })`, while `buildOrderFilterSearchParams()` deletes `status` whenever `quick` is present. The displayed quick-card count can therefore be status-scoped, but the click destination is the global quick queue.

Quick-card counts therefore match the global quick queue opened by `OrderManagement.handleQuickFilterChange(...)`. No build or automated tests were run per instruction.
- Expected fix direction: Either compute quick summary cards in the same global scope used by the click destination, or preserve/encode the active status scope when opening a quick filter; the UI should also label scoped counts clearly if both dimensions remain active.

### F198: Dashboard logistics coverage divides shipped orders by all tracked orders

- Status: FIXED
- Evidence: Static verification at 2026-05-30 10:44 UTC found `AdminController.getDashboard()` counting `shippedOrders` only when `order.status == SHIPPED`, but counting `ordersWithTracking` for every order with a nonblank tracking number regardless of status. Frontend `AdminDashboard.tsx` computes `trackingCoverage = ordersWithTracking / shippedOrders` and clamps it to 100, while missing-tracking count is `SHIPPED`-scoped. Historical completed/returned tracked orders can therefore inflate coverage and make `With tracking` exceed `Shipped orders` beside a non-zero missing-tracking warning.
- Retest: 2026-05-31 20:14 UTC static source review found `AdminController.getDashboard()` now builds `currentlyShippedOrders` first, then computes `shippedOrders`, `ordersWithTracking`, and `ordersWithoutTracking` from that same `SHIPPED`-only list. No build or automated tests were run per instruction.
- Expected fix direction: Use the same `SHIPPED` scope for both numerator and denominator, or rename/split the metrics so historical tracked orders are not presented as current shipped-order coverage.

### F192: Alert search treats empty severity/category filters as WARNING and APPLICATION

- Status: FIXED

IS NULL OR severity = ?)` and `(? IS NULL OR category = ?)`. ### F191: Single alert acknowledge API can regress resolved alerts back to acknowledged

- Status: FIXED

### F173: Manual controller errors bypass the shared API error envelope

- Status: FIXED
- Evidence: `GlobalApiExceptionHandler`/`ApiErrorResponseFactory` produce a shared envelope with `error`, `message`, status metadata, path, request id, and timestamp, and frontend `getApiErrorMessage()` reads both `error` and `message`. Rechecked at 2026-05-30 08:59 UTC: multiple controllers still manually return `Map.of("error", ...)`, omitting the shared metadata and `message` field.
- Retest: 2026-06-01 06:03 UTC static source review confirmed `ManualApiErrorResponseAdvice` now intercepts JSON-like controller `Map` bodies that contain `error` but miss shared envelope fields, rebuilds the payload through `ApiErrorResponseFactory`, preserves extra fields, and forces a bad-request status if a manual error body somehow leaves with a non-error status. Existing manual `Map.of("error", ...)` controller paths therefore serialize with `message`, `status`, `statusText`, `path`, `requestId`, and `timestamp` without controller-by-controller rewrites. No build, automated test, screenshot, video, trace, or commit was run per instruction.
- Expected fix direction: Route manual bad-request/error responses through the shared `ApiErrorResponseFactory` or throw handled exceptions consistently.

### F167: Product URL import has DNS rebinding SSRF risk despite private-IP validation

- Status: FIXED
- Evidence: Rechecked at 2026-05-30 08:59 UTC: `ProductUrlImportService.normalizeAndValidateUri()` already blocks non-http(s), credentials, non-standard ports, and hosts resolving to local/private/link-local/multicast addresses. The remaining risk is DNS rebinding/time-of-check-to-time-of-use because validation resolves the host before `HttpClient` performs its own DNS resolution for the fetch.
- Expected fix direction: Pin resolved addresses or otherwise verify the actual outbound connection target after DNS resolution, including redirects and dynamic fallback fetches.
- Retest: 2026-05-31 21:20 UTC static source review found `ProductUrlImportService` now creates a public DNS pin snapshot for each outbound import request. `fetchHtml(...)` and `sendTopmRequest(...)` resolve and validate the host address set immediately before sending, then call `DnsPin.verifyUnchanged()` after the response; any changed address set or newly blocked private/local/multicast address rejects the import. Redirect targets, nested `goods_url` fallback fetches, and TOPM dynamic POST/GET endpoints all pass through those guarded paths. No build or automated test was run per instruction.

## Resolved Issues

### F407: Native App bottom rail leaves a large blank area after hiding the support tab

- Area: Frontend / Native App bottom navigation
- Environment: Android WebView-like native App shell with five visible bottom-rail actions
- Steps: Open the native App storefront and inspect the fixed bottom navigation rail after the App-specific support tab is hidden.
- Expected: The five visible actions should occupy five equal columns across the full rail, with the account action aligned to the far-right slot and no unused blank column.
- Actual: The footer workbench visually showed five buttons, but the right side of the rail had a large empty area because the App CSS relied on positional child hiding while later bottom-rail overrides could leave the visible items out of the intended five-column placement.
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Added semantic bottom-rail item classes in `Navbar.tsx`, hid the App support tab by class in `mobile-app.css`, pinned the remaining Home/Products/Coupons/Cart/Account actions to five equal grid columns, and forced visible items to stretch to their grid cells. Follow-up hardening makes native App mode omit the footer support tab from the DOM, adds a `shop-nav__bottomBar--native` five-area layout, and replaces the older positional `nth-child(5)` App hide rule with semantic support-tab hiding so Account cannot be mistaken for the removed support slot. The floating App support launcher remains available.
- Retest: 2026-05-31 17:57 UTC static source review confirmed the semantic class wiring and final App-only CSS override. No build, automated test, screenshot, video, or trace was run in this pass.
- Retest: 2026-05-31 18:20 UTC no-screenshot Playwright DOM/layout probe at Android WebView-like `390x844` and `360x800` confirmed five bottom-item DOM nodes, five visible items, no support DOM node, equal five-column grid (`maxWidthDelta` <= 0.01px), Account in the far-right slot with only 4-6px rail padding to the right edge, and `scrollWidth == clientWidth`. `git diff --check` for the touched nav files and `npx tsc --noEmit --pretty false` both passed.

### F133: Public payment channel response exposes provider implementation details

- Area: Backend / Payment channels; Frontend / checkout payment typing
- Environment: Public `/payments/channels` used by checkout, profile payment recovery, and payment component
- Steps: Inspect enabled channel JSON from `/payments/channels`
- Expected: Public channel data contains only checkout display and recommendation fields
- Actual: Public channel data included `provider` and `refundMode`, exposing payment adapter and refund-mode internals that the storefront did not use
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Removed `provider` and `refundMode` from `PaymentChannelResponse` and frontend `PaymentChannel`; server-side payment/refund configuration remains internal.

### F132: Frontend exposes unimplemented guest cart quote route

- Area: Frontend / cart API contract; Backend / route parity
- Environment: Future guest cart quote or checkout wiring using `/cart/guest/quote`
- Steps: Compare frontend `cartApi.quoteGuestItems()` with backend `CartController` mappings
- Expected: Exported cart helpers correspond to implemented backend routes
- Actual: The frontend exported a helper for `/cart/guest/quote`, but no backend route existed and current pages did not use it
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Removed the unused helper so no frontend API contract advertises the missing route.

### F131: Frontend public coupon contract still models admin coupon fields

- Area: Frontend / Coupon Center and coupon API typing
- Environment: Public coupon center reads through `/coupons/public`
- Steps: Compare frontend public coupon types/helpers with backend `CouponPublicResponse`
- Expected: Public coupon frontend state models only public response fields and does not depend on admin-only coupon metadata
- Actual: `couponApi.getPublic()` and Coupon Center helpers used full `Coupon` typing, including `scope`, `status`, `totalQuantity`, and `claimedQuantity`
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Added `CouponPublic`, typed public coupon API/cache/page/helpers with it, and changed public fallback/test data to use `remainingQuantity` while preserving full `Coupon` for admin management.

### F130: Frontend exposes unimplemented membership API routes

- Area: Frontend / API contract; Backend / route parity
- Environment: Future membership UI or QA route coverage using `/membership/plans`, `/membership/me`, or `/membership/orders`
- Steps: Compare frontend `membershipApi` exports with backend route mappings and schema
- Expected: Exported commercial feature APIs have matching implemented backend routes, or the unfinished feature remains hidden
- Actual: The frontend exported `membershipApi` and membership types, but no backend membership controller/service/schema existed
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Removed the unused frontend membership API export and orphaned membership types so the app no longer exposes guaranteed-404 membership routes.

### F129: Pet gallery quota response exposes account and IP upload counters

- Area: Backend / Pet Gallery; Frontend / quota API contract
- Environment: Signed-in Home and Pet Gallery upload readiness checks through `GET /pet-gallery/quota`
- Steps: Load the pet-gallery upload UI as a signed-in customer and inspect the quota JSON
- Expected: Quota response includes only upload limit, remaining uploads, and whether upload is allowed
- Actual: Quota response included `userUploads` and `ipUploads`, exposing internal account/IP anti-abuse counters that the storefront did not need
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Removed account/IP upload counters from `PetGalleryQuota` and frontend quota typing while keeping the backend account/IP remaining-quota calculation server-side.

### F128: Customer review submit response exposes raw review entity

- Area: Backend / Reviews; Frontend / review API contract
- Environment: Signed-in product detail review submission
- Steps: Submit a product review through `POST /reviews/product/{productId}` and inspect the response JSON
- Expected: Submit response uses the same narrowed storefront review DTO as public reads
- Actual: Submit response returned raw `Review`, including internal user/order/moderation/entity-derived fields not needed by the storefront
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Mapped saved reviews through `PublicReviewResponse.from(...)` in the customer submit endpoint and typed `reviewApi.create` as `PublicReview`. Admin review queue, reply, and status endpoints keep full `Review` for moderation.

### F127: Logistics tracking response exposes raw provider payload

- Area: Backend / Logistics; Frontend / tracking widget contract
- Environment: Customer, guest, and admin logistics tracking through `/logistics/track`
- Steps: Query logistics tracking with a configured provider and inspect the response payload/UI states
- Expected: Tracking responses include only normalized display fields and events, without third-party raw provider bodies
- Actual: `LogisticsTrackResponse` included `rawResponse`, and frontend types/copy still modeled raw provider data
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Removed `rawResponse` from backend DTO/service population, narrowed frontend logistics response typing, and removed stale raw-provider locale/test mock copy. Empty tracking states now depend on normalized events/status/summary only.

### F126: Customer product-question submit response exposes raw question entity

- Area: Backend / Product questions; Frontend / question API contract
- Environment: Signed-in product detail Q&A submission
- Steps: Submit a question through `POST /product-questions/product/{productId}` and inspect the response JSON
- Expected: Submit response uses the same narrowed storefront question DTO as public reads
- Actual: Submit response returned raw `ProductQuestion`, including customer/moderation/product entity-derived fields not needed by the storefront
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Mapped ask responses through `ProductQuestionPublicResponse`; admin queue and answer endpoints keep full `ProductQuestion` for moderation.

### F125: Customer and guest order APIs expose raw order entities

- Area: Backend / Orders and order tracking; Frontend / order API contract
- Environment: Customer profile order center, guest checkout/order tracking, support order context, and order item reads
- Steps: Load `/orders/me`, `/orders/{id}`, `/orders/guest/{id}`, order item routes, checkout responses, or `/orders/track` and inspect returned JSON
- Expected: Storefront order responses include only customer-facing order summary, payment, shipping, tracking, return, and item display fields
- Actual: Raw `Order` and `OrderItem` entities exposed internal owner `userId`, coupon linkage ids, item `orderId`, guest email embedded in shippingAddress, and update metadata to storefront callers
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Added `OrderCustomerResponse` and `OrderItemCustomerResponse`, mapped customer/guest order reads and checkout results through them, and made public tracking return the same narrowed DTOs via `OrderTrackResponse`. Admin order APIs and admin-visible compatibility paths keep full entity data for operations.

### F124: Public category APIs expose raw category entity and missing by-id route

- Area: Backend / Categories; Frontend / category API contract
- Environment: Storefront category navigation, homepage discovery, product filters, and future category detail reads
- Steps: Inspect `/categories` or call frontend `categoryApi.getById(id)`
- Expected: Public category reads return a stable storefront DTO and `/categories/{id}` is available with the same safe contract
- Actual: Public category list returned raw `Category` entities, and the frontend-declared by-id route was missing in the backend
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Added `CategoryPublicResponse`, mapped public list/top-level/children/by-id category reads through it, enriched by-id with public productCount, and typed frontend category reads as `CategoryPublic`. Admin category create/update/delete still use the existing `Category` payload contract.

### F123: Customer support responses expose account and assignment identifiers

- Area: Backend / Support REST and WebSocket; Frontend / support types
- Environment: Customer support widget, guest order support, and admin support queue
- Steps: Load customer/guest support session/messages or inspect customer WebSocket support payloads
- Expected: Customer support payloads include only conversation display fields and no account/admin assignment identifiers
- Actual: Raw `SupportSession` and `SupportMessage` payloads exposed `userId`, `assignedAdminId`, `contextKey`, `senderId`, and admin read-state fields to customer/guest support clients
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Added customer support session/message DTOs, mapped customer and guest REST responses through them, and split WebSocket broadcast payloads so customer sockets receive narrowed DTOs while admin sockets keep the full queue-management contract. Customer `CONNECTED` WebSocket messages no longer include `userId`, and frontend support id fields are optional for compatibility.

### F122: Public product APIs expose raw product entity fields

- Area: Backend / ProductController, SearchController, PageController; Frontend / product API contract
- Environment: Storefront product list/detail/search/home aliases, recommendations, finder candidates, add-on candidates, by-ids, featured, and personalized recommendations
- Steps: Inspect public product JSON from `/products`, `/products/{id}`, `/products/featured`, `/products/by-ids`, `/products/{id}/recommendations`, `/products/add-on-candidates`, `/products/finder-candidates`, `/products/personalized-recommendations`, `/search`, or `/home/products`
- Expected: Public product responses expose only storefront display and purchase fields, while backend status and audit timestamps remain admin-only
- Actual: Public product endpoints returned raw `Product` entities, exposing fields such as `status`, `createdAt`, and `updatedAt`
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Added `ProductPublicResponse` and mapped all public product reads, search, and home-product aliases through it. The DTO preserves storefront display, option-selection, bundle, promotion, review, and purchase fields while omitting raw entity status/timestamps; admin product management keeps full `Product`.

### F121: Customer notification APIs expose owner userId

- Area: Backend / Notifications; Frontend / notification types
- Environment: Signed-in storefront notification center
- Steps: Load `/notifications/me` as a customer and inspect the response payload
- Expected: Customer responses include only notification display/read fields and do not include owner `userId`
- Actual: Raw `Notification` entities were returned, so `userId` appeared in notification JSON
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Added `NotificationResponse`, mapped notification list responses through it, and made frontend `AppNotification.userId` optional for compatibility. Read/unread-count/delete paths continue to enforce ownership through server-side entity lookups.

### F120: Cart and wishlist customer APIs expose owner userId

- Area: Backend / Cart, wishlist and favorites aliases; Frontend / cart and wishlist types
- Environment: Signed-in storefront cart and wishlist pages
- Steps: Load `/cart/me`, `/wishlist/me`, or `/favorites` as a customer and inspect the response payload
- Expected: Customer responses include only cart/wishlist item display fields and do not include owner `userId`
- Actual: Raw `CartItem` and `Wishlist` entities were returned, so `userId` appeared in customer cart/wishlist JSON
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Added `CartItemResponse` and `WishlistItemResponse`, mapped cart list and wishlist/favorites list responses through those DTOs, and made frontend `CartItem.userId` / `WishlistItem.userId` optional for compatibility. Mutations continue to enforce ownership using server-side entity lookups.

### F119: Public brand API exposes admin metadata and admin brand list route is missing

- Area: Backend / BrandController, AdminController; Frontend / brandApi, BrandManagement, ProductManagement
- Environment: Public `/brands` and admin brand management `/admin/brands`
- Steps: Inspect public brand JSON and open Brand Management after it calls `adminApi.getBrands()`
- Expected: Public brand reads contain only active storefront display fields, while admin brand management has an authenticated full-list route
- Actual: Public `/brands` returned raw `Brand` rows with admin metadata, and `/admin/brands` was not defined even though the frontend admin page requested it
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Added `BrandPublicResponse` for public `/brands`, restricted public reads to active display fields, added `/admin/brands` to `AdminController` for full brand inventory under existing admin brand permission, and updated frontend public brand typing to `BrandPublic`.

### F118: Customer address APIs expose userId in customer responses

- Area: Backend / User addresses; Frontend / address types
- Environment: Signed-in customer address book, default-address lookup, address create/update responses, and legacy `/user/addresses` alias
- Steps: Load `/addresses/me`, `/addresses/{id}`, `/addresses/me/default`, or save an address as a customer and inspect the JSON response
- Expected: Customer address responses expose only address display/editing fields and do not include the owner user id
- Actual: Raw `UserAddress` entities were returned, so `userId` appeared in customer address responses
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Added `UserAddressResponse` and mapped customer address endpoints plus `/user/addresses` through it. Create/update responses now re-read the persisted address before mapping, preserving generated ids/timestamps/default state while hiding `userId`. Frontend `UserAddress.userId` is optional for compatibility with any remaining admin or legacy data shapes.

### F117: Public announcement API exposes admin scheduling and status fields

- Area: Backend / Site announcements; Frontend / Navbar announcement banner
- Environment: Public `GET /announcements/active` storefront banner data
- Steps: Inspect the public active-announcement response for fields beyond banner display data
- Expected: Public responses contain only id, title, content, and a sanitized link URL
- Actual: Raw `SiteAnnouncement` entities exposed admin fields such as status, sortOrder, startsAt, endsAt, createdAt, and updatedAt
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Added `SiteAnnouncementPublicResponse`, mapped active announcement reads through it after safe-link filtering, and updated frontend public announcement typing. Admin announcement APIs still use the full announcement entity for scheduling and management.

### F116: Frontend user-scoped caches can survive account switch

- Area: Frontend / API cache layer and auth session helpers
- Environment: Same browser switching between accounts without a full reload
- Steps: Load account-scoped data such as addresses, available coupons, notifications, gallery state, or order items as one user, then sign in as another user before cache TTL expiry
- Expected: Account-scoped cache entries are scoped to the current user and cleared when the account or role changes
- Actual: Several frontend caches used fixed keys such as `list`, `default`, `mine`, `available`, or `auth`, and some login/logout paths bypassed shared auth cleanup
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Added current-user cache scoping for affected frontend caches, centralized session persistence/cleanup through `persistAuthSession` and `clearStoredAuthSession`, and wired Login, Navbar, AdminLayout, useAuth, and Checkout auth-expiry cleanup through those helpers.

### F115: Public brand API wrapper ignores active-only filtering

- Area: Frontend / brandApi
- Environment: Frontend calls to `brandApi.getAll({ activeOnly: true })`
- Steps: Inactivate a brand, then inspect the `/brands` request from active-only callers
- Expected: Active-only calls pass `activeOnly=true` and do not show inactive brands
- Actual: The API wrapper ignored the option and requested `/brands` without params, returning all brands
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Public `brandApi.getAll()` now defaults to active-only reads, explicit `activeOnly:false` uses a separate all-brand cache, and BrandManagement now loads full inventory through `adminApi.getBrands()`.

### F114: Checkout discount coupon preview uses the wrong percent semantics

- Area: Frontend / Checkout
- Environment: Signed-in checkout with percentage coupons
- Steps: Compare frontend estimated savings for a `DISCOUNT` coupon with backend coupon calculation
- Expected: Frontend and backend both treat `discountPercent` as payable percent, so 80 means 20% off
- Actual: Checkout estimated percentage coupons as `subtotal * percent / 100`, making 80 look like 80% off instead of 20% off
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Checkout coupon estimation and next-unlock hints now calculate percentage discounts as `subtotal * (100 - payablePercent) / 100`, matching backend `CouponService`.

### F113: Customer coupon APIs expose raw coupon and user-coupon entities

- Area: Backend / CouponController, CouponService, CouponQuoteResponse; Frontend / coupon types
- Environment: Coupon center, wallet, claim, available-coupon, and checkout quote APIs
- Steps: Inspect public coupon and signed-in coupon JSON responses
- Expected: Storefront/customer APIs expose only display and usage fields required by the UI
- Actual: Public APIs returned raw `Coupon`; customer APIs returned raw `UserCoupon`, including operational and ownership fields such as `userId`, `orderId`, `couponScope`, and backend coupon status
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Added `CouponPublicResponse` and `UserCouponResponse`. Public coupons expose safe campaign data plus `remainingQuantity`; customer coupon and quote responses expose only the user's coupon id, coupon id, status/timestamps, display rule, validity window, and description.

### F112: Customer profile API returns the full user entity

- Area: Backend / UserController; Frontend / userApi
- Environment: Signed-in `/users/profile` calls used across storefront profile/auth and admin permission checks
- Steps: Call `/users/profile` while authenticated and inspect the response fields
- Expected: Self-profile response exposes only identity/contact and authorization fields needed by the frontend
- Actual: The endpoint returned raw `User`, exposing unrelated entity fields such as address/status/timestamps and making future entity fields part of the customer contract by default
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Added `UserProfileResponse` and changed `/users/profile` to return the safe DTO. Frontend `UserProfile` and `userApi.getProfile` now match that narrowed contract.

### F111: Public pet gallery responses expose upload owner and file metadata

- Area: Backend / Pet Gallery; Frontend / PetGallery, API types
- Environment: Public `/pet-gallery` list, upload, and like responses
- Steps: Inspect the public gallery JSON response for uploaded or seeded photos
- Expected: Public gallery data contains only storefront display fields and viewer flags, not uploader account IDs, client IPs, file metadata, or internal moderation/source state
- Actual: Raw `PetGalleryPhoto` entities were returned publicly, exposing fields such as `userId`, `ipAddress`, `originalFilename`, `contentType`, `fileSize`, `status`, and `source`. Logged-in users could also reuse the anonymous gallery cache, causing stale `canDelete` and viewer like state.
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Public gallery endpoints now return `PetGalleryPhotoPublicResponse` with id, masked/curated username, imageUrl, likeCount, likedByMe, canDelete, and createdAt only. Frontend public gallery types were narrowed, and gallery cache keys are separated for anonymous and signed-in reads.

### F110: Customer and guest payment APIs expose gateway/internal payment references

- Area: Backend / PaymentController; Frontend / paymentApi, OrderManagement
- Environment: Customer payment creation, recovery, sync, guest payment lookup, callback response, and admin payment history
- Steps: Create or recover a payment as a customer/guest and inspect payment endpoint responses
- Expected: Customer/guest responses include only checkout-safe payment data; gateway provider references, refund references, and callback metadata remain admin-only, and failed guest payment probes feed blacklist counters
- Actual: Shared `Payment` entities were returned to storefront and callback callers, exposing fields such as `providerReference`, `refundReference`, and `callbackAt`
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Added `PaymentResponse` for non-admin payment responses. Customer and guest payment create/sync/history/latest endpoints now return safe DTOs, callbacks return `{received:true}`, failed guest payment lookups record payment blacklist failures, and admin order management uses explicit admin payment helpers with `AdminPayment` for full operational fields.

### F109: Reviewable-order lookup exposes more order data than the product review form needs

- Area: Backend / Product reviews; Frontend / ProductDetail, ProductReview
- Environment: Signed-in product detail review composer and `GET /reviews/product/{productId}/reviewable-orders`
- Steps: Open a product page as a signed-in customer with completed orders and inspect the reviewable order selector response
- Expected: The helper endpoint returns only the minimum fields required to choose the order being reviewed, remains explicitly authenticated, and keeps review helper lists bounded
- Actual: The endpoint returned full `Order` objects even though the UI only needed order id/order number/date labels, and the public review list had no configured row cap. Signed-in review fetches could also reuse the anonymous review cache and miss owner-only pending reviews.
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Added `ReviewableOrderResponse` with only id, orderNo, createdAt, and completedAt; added an explicit authenticated security matcher for `/reviews/product/*/reviewable-orders`; capped public review rows with `review.public-max-rows` and reviewable-order rows with `review.reviewable-order-max-rows`; and made signed-in review loads bypass the anonymous review cache.

### F108: Public product reviews expose internal user/order/moderation fields

- Area: Backend / Product reviews; Frontend / ProductDetail, ProductReview
- Environment: Public product review section and review alias endpoints
- Steps: Inspect `GET /reviews/product/{productId}` or `GET /products/{productId}/reviews` for a product with reviews
- Expected: Public review responses expose only display-safe review content and masked customer identity; internal user/order/moderation fields remain admin-only
- Actual: Public review endpoints returned raw `Review` entities, including fields such as `userId`, `orderId`, `status`, and product payloads that are not needed on the storefront
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Public review reads now return `PublicReviewResponse` with only id, productId, rating, comment, masked username, merchant reply, timestamps, and `editableByCurrentUser`. Frontend storefront review types now consume `PublicReview`; admin review pages still use the full `Review` contract.

### F107: Public product questions expose unanswered content and customer identifiers

- Area: Backend / Product questions; Frontend / ProductDetail
- Environment: Public product detail Q&A section
- Steps: Ask a product question and view the product page before an admin answers it
- Expected: Public product page shows only answered/merchant-reviewed Q&A and no customer identifiers; answering is handled in admin
- Actual: Public endpoint returned raw question entities, including unanswered questions and `userId`/`username`, and the product page rendered an answer form
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Public product question reads now use `ProductQuestionPublicResponse` and only return answered rows, capped by `product-question.public-max-rows`. The product page only displays public question text, date and merchant answer. The customer-side answer API was removed from `questionApi`, tests now use `adminApi.answerQuestion`, and the obsolete `/product-questions/{id}/answer` backend route plus permission/interceptor mappings were removed.

### F106: Public order tracking exposes registered-account order details through order number and email

- Area: Backend / OrderService, OrderTrackResponse; Frontend / OrderTracking.tsx
- Environment: Public `GET /orders/track` for registered-account orders
- Steps: Use a registered customer's order number and checkout email in public order tracking
- Expected: Public lookup reveals only low-sensitivity status; full registered-account order details require sign-in
- Actual: Public tracking returned the complete order object and order items, including address, payment, shipment, return and item details
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Registered-account public tracking responses now set `detailsRestricted=true` and include only a minimal order status summary with no item rows or sensitive order fields. The frontend renders a login prompt and status-only summary, while true guest orders keep the existing full public tracking flow.

### F105: Sensitive public credential endpoints do not consistently feed IP blacklist operations

- Area: Backend / IP blacklist, auth, guest order, guest support
- Environment: Public forgot-password, admin bootstrap, guest order and guest support endpoints
- Steps: Submit repeated wrong credentials or mismatched guest session/order values
- Expected: Repeated failures are visible in IP blacklist management and can trigger/release blocks
- Actual: Several public credential-style endpoints were outside the default protected path list or did not record failures into the blacklist service
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Default `security.ip-blacklist.path-prefixes` and the config-center template now include `/auth/forgot-password`, `/auth/register`, `/auth/refresh`, `/users/create-admin`, `/orders/track`, `/orders/guest`, and `/support/guest` in addition to login/payment/guest-checkout paths. Controllers now record specific LOGIN-source failure reasons for forgot-password, admin bootstrap, guest order credential/action, and guest support order/session failures.

### F104: Guest checkout email can be claimed as a registered account without verifying mailbox ownership

- Area: Backend / AuthController, UserService; Frontend / Register.tsx
- Environment: `POST /auth/register` after a guest checkout created a `GUEST` user for the same email
- Steps: Know a guest checkout email and register a new account with that email
- Expected: Converting a `GUEST` account into a registered account requires proving mailbox ownership first
- Actual: Registration could upgrade the reused guest email account without an email-code challenge
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Guest-email claims now require a valid 6-digit code verified by `EmailLoginService` before `UserService.register(..., guestEmailVerified=true)` can upgrade the account. The frontend reacts to `emailCodeRequired`, shows the code input and send-code action, and submits the code with registration. Register email-code failures are recorded with a register-specific reason for blacklist/audit clarity.

### F103: Anonymous pet-gallery likes are not database-idempotent under concurrency

- Area: Backend / PetGalleryService, PetGalleryPhotoLike; Schema / pet_gallery_photo_likes
- Environment: Public `POST /pet-gallery/{id}/like`
- Steps: Send concurrent anonymous like requests for the same photo from the same client IP
- Expected: One viewer can increase a photo's like count only once
- Actual: Anonymous de-duplication used a service-level pre-check by IP, but the database unique key only covered `(photo_id, user_id)`, allowing concurrent null-user inserts
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Pet-gallery likes now store a required `viewerKey` and enforce unique `(photo_id, viewer_key)`. Startup schema hardening backfills old rows, removes duplicate historical rows, recalibrates historical `like_count` from de-duplicated like rows, and adds the new index/constraint.

### F102: Guest support sessions can mix messages across orders for the same guest email

- Area: Backend / SupportController, SupportService, SupportSessionMapper; Schema / support_sessions
- Environment: Multiple guest orders created with the same guest email
- Steps: Open support on one guest order, then use another guest order for the same email to load/send guest support messages
- Expected: Guest support access is scoped to the verified order context
- Actual: Support sessions were keyed only by reused guest `user_id`, so support history could be shared across orders for the same guest email
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Guest support sessions now use `contextKey=guest-order:{orderNo}` and access checks require both the guest user and order context to match. Existing signed-in support remains unchanged with null/blank context, and normal support lists, unread counts, REST access, and WebSocket access are restricted to that null/blank context so guest-order sessions cannot be reached through ordinary user support APIs.

### F93: WebSocket URL missing token parameter (test mismatch)

- Area: Frontend / api/index.ts
- Environment: Frontend test (api/index.test.ts)
- Steps: Run `supportWebSocketUrl('token')` and check URL
- Expected: URL contains `?token=token` query parameter
- Actual: URL does not contain token (token moved to subprotocol per B16 fix)
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Updated frontend tests to assert token-free WebSocket URLs plus `support.v1` / `auth.<base64url-token>` protocols. Customer and admin support WebSocket clients now pass those protocols, and the backend support handler reads JWTs from `Sec-WebSocket-Protocol` while preserving legacy query-token compatibility.

### F94: Auth storage not cleared on 401 error

- Area: Frontend / api/index.ts
- Environment: Frontend test (api/index.test.ts)
- Steps: Trigger 401 error without refresh token, check localStorage
- Expected: `localStorage.getItem('token')` returns null
- Actual: Returns "7" (storage not cleared)
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Expanded shared auth-session cleanup to remove `userId`, `username`, `role`, and `adminDefaultPath` along with token data.

### F95: IP blacklist empty list prevents management

- Area: Frontend / IpBlacklistManagement.tsx
- Environment: Admin IP blacklist center
- Steps: Open IP blacklist management when there are no blocked rows
- Expected: Admin can manually block an IP, clear filters, and understand the empty state
- Actual: The default blocked-only empty list made the page feel unmanageable
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: Defaulted the page to all records, added an operational notice, localized status/source filters, added reset filters, and added empty-state actions for manual block and showing all records. Follow-up root-cause fixes: backend source filtering no longer treats empty/ALL as MANUAL, invalid/empty status filters no longer produce empty queries, automatic LOGIN/PAYMENT entries show in the list, status includes total/released counts, refresh/search/Enter handlers no longer pass React events as query overrides, dropdown changes reload immediately, manual block/reset reload the full list, old `ip_blacklist_entries` tables are hardened on startup, row mapping tolerates missing non-core columns during rollout, and frontend list rendering no longer depends on the status-summary request succeeding.

### F96: Admin review management can render empty because review API contract is inconsistent

- Area: Backend / AdminController reviews, Frontend / ReviewManagement.tsx
- Environment: Admin review management
- Steps: Open review management after frontend expects `AdminReviewPage.items` while backend returns raw `List<Review>`
- Expected: Review table loads real rows and supports reliable status/search pagination
- Actual: The page could show an empty table despite review data, and local-only filters could miss records outside the loaded page
- Status: Fixed
- Resolution: `/admin/reviews` now returns a paginated page object with totals and status summary, backend supports status/search filters, frontend uses service-side pagination, and API normalization still accepts legacy raw-array responses.

F93, F94, F95, and F96 fixed in code. See QA_ISSUES.md for full history.

- i18n: EN/ZH/ES locales complete with 2776 keys each

Frontend dev service on port 3000 was restarted and returned HTTP 200.
- 2026-06-02 13:35 UTC: **UI/accessibility issues fixed.** Navbar and product-list search submit controls now use real Ant Design `Button` elements with accessible names. Product-list pagination previous/next controls now receive localized accessible names. Product-detail breadcrumb home control and mobile thumbnail buttons now have accessible labels/titles. Mobile product-detail carousel arrows now have at least 44px touch targets.
- 2026-06-02 13:35 UTC: **Upload media path regression fixed.** `resolveApiAssetUrl` no longer rewrites `/uploads/...` and `uploads/...` into `/api/uploads/...`; upload assets remain same-origin `/uploads/...`. Added/update tests for that behavior.
- 2026-06-02 13:35 UTC: **Pet gallery upload-image 404 fixed.** Root cause was Nginx location precedence: the generic static image extension rule intercepted `/uploads/...webp` before the uploads proxy. Updated live Nginx and deploy templates to use `location ^~ /uploads/`, then reloaded Nginx. Source-origin and public cache-busted upload URLs returned 200 image/webp. Public pet-gallery API now appends a stable `?v=...` parameter to local upload image URLs to bypass stale Cloudflare 404 cache entries. Added DTO and service coverage for local upload visibility/cache behavior.
- 2026-06-02 13:35 UTC: **No-screenshot E2E/smoke regression passed.** Playwright DOM/network smoke covered desktop 1366x900 and mobile 390x844 across `/`, `/products`, product detail, `/pet-gallery`, `/cart`, `/checkout`, `/coupons`, `/login`, `/register`, `/profile`, `/wishlist`, and `/track-order`. Final result: passed with zero issues. Navigation-time `ERR_ABORTED` cancellations were treated as noise; real 4xx/5xx and rendered broken image checks passed.
